        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr style="font-size:85%;">
        <td style="width:1.0em; padding:0.4em 0 0 0.6em;">
         a.
        </td>
        <td colspan="2" style="padding-left:0;text-align:left;">
         <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_name_transl">
          <b>
           <a href="#ref_name_transl">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
          Since the Western Roman Empire was not a distinct state separate from the Eastern Roman Empire, there was no particular official term that designated the Western provinces or their government, which was simply known as the "Roman Empire". Terms such as
          <i>
           Imperium Romanum Occidentalis
          </i>
          and
          <i>
           Hesperium Imperium
          </i>
          were either never in official usage or invented long after the western court had fallen.
         </span>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr class="mergedbottomrow" style="font-size:85%;">
        <td style="width:1.0em; padding:0 0 0 0.6em;">
         b.
        </td>
        <td colspan="2" style="padding-left:0;text-align:left;">
         <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_lifespan">
          <b>
           <a href="#ref_lifespan">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
          Whilst the deposition of
          <a href="/wiki/Romulus_Augustulus" title="Romulus Augustulus">
           Romulus Augustulus
          </a>
          in
          <b>
           476
          </b>
          is the most commonly cited end date for the Western Roman Empire, the last Western Roman Emperor
          <a href="/wiki/Julius_Nepos" title="Julius Nepos">
           Julius Nepos
          </a>
          did not die until
          <b>
           480
          </b>
          , when the title and notion of a separate Western Empire were actually abolished. Other suggested end dates include the deposition of
          <a href="/wiki/Glycerius" title="Glycerius">
           Glycerius
          </a>
          in
          <b>
           474
          </b>
          and the reorganization of Italy and abolition of separate Western Roman administrative institutions under
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Justinian" title="Justinian">
           Justinian
          </a>
          in
          <b>
           554
          </b>
          .
         </span>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Historiography" title="Historiography">
        historiography
       </a>
       , the
       <b>
        Western Roman Empire
       </b>
       consists of the western provinces of the
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">
        Roman Empire
       </a>
       at any one time during which they were administered by a separate independent Imperial court, coequal with (or only nominally subordinate to) that administering the eastern half. Both "Western Roman Empire" and "Eastern Roman Empire" (or "
       <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">
        Byzantine Empire
       </a>
       ") are modern terms describing
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">
         de facto
        </a>
       </i>
       independent
       <a href="/wiki/Polity" title="Polity">
        entities
       </a>
       ; however, at no point did the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancient_Romans" title="Ancient Romans">
        Romans
       </a>
       consider the Empire split into two, but rather considered it a single state governed by two separate Imperial courts out of administrative expediency, a system of government known as a
       <a href="/wiki/Diarchy" title="Diarchy">
        diarchy
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The view that the Empire was impossible to govern by one
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_emperor" title="Roman emperor">
        emperor
       </a>
       was established by
       <a href="/wiki/Diocletian" title="Diocletian">
        Diocletian
       </a>
       following the disastrous civil wars and disintegration of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crisis_of_the_3rd_century" title="Crisis of the 3rd century">
        Crisis of the 3rd century
       </a>
       , and was instituted in Roman law by his introduction of the
       <a href="/wiki/Tetrarchy" title="Tetrarchy">
        Tetrarchy
       </a>
       in AD 285, a form of government which was legally to endure in one form or another for centuries. There being more than one emperor at a time was not an unknown concept in the empire, as there had been multiple points in the past where more than one emperor ruled jointly. The Western Court was periodically abolished and recreated for the next two centuries until final abolition by
       <a href="/wiki/Zeno_(emperor)" title="Zeno (emperor)">
        Zeno
       </a>
       in 480, by which time there was little effective central control left in the area legally administered by the Western Court.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Western Roman Empire existed intermittently in several periods between the 3rd and 5th centuries, after Diocletian's
       <a href="/wiki/Tetrarchy" title="Tetrarchy">
        Tetrarchy
       </a>
       and the reunifications associated with
       <a href="/wiki/Constantine_the_Great" title="Constantine the Great">
        Constantine the Great
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Julian_the_Apostate" title="Julian the Apostate">
        Julian the Apostate
       </a>
       (331/2–363).
       <a href="/wiki/Theodosius_I" title="Theodosius I">
        Theodosius I
       </a>
       divided the Empire upon his death (in 395) between his two sons. Finally, eighty-five years later, Zeno of the Eastern Empire recognized the reality of the Western Empire's reduced domain—Roman power ceased to exist even in the Italian Peninsula—after the deposition of
       <a href="/wiki/Romulus_Augustulus" title="Romulus Augustulus">
        Romulus Augustus
       </a>
       and the subsequent death of
       <a href="/wiki/Julius_Nepos" title="Julius Nepos">
        Julius Nepos
       </a>
       , and therefore proclaimed himself the sole emperor of the Roman Empire.
      </p>
      <p>
       The rise of
       <a href="/wiki/Odoacer" title="Odoacer">
        Odoacer
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Foederati" title="Foederati">
        Foederati
       </a>
       to rule over Italy in 476 was popularized by eighteenth-century historian
       <a href="/wiki/Edward_Gibbon" title="Edward Gibbon">
        Edward Gibbon
       </a>
       as a demarcating event for the
       <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_the_Western_Roman_Empire" title="Fall of the Western Roman Empire">
        end of the Western Empire
       </a>
       and is sometimes used to mark the transition from
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Classical_Antiquity" title="Classical Antiquity">
        Antiquity
       </a>
       to the
       <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">
        Middle Ages
       </a>
       . Imperial rule was reimposed in large parts of the West, including
       <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">
        North Africa
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Italy" title="Roman Italy">
        Italy
       </a>
       and parts of
       <a href="/wiki/Hispania" title="Hispania">
        Hispania
       </a>
       , in the sixth century by the armies of the Eastern Roman Empire under Emperor
       <a href="/wiki/Justinian_I" title="Justinian I">
        Justinian I
       </a>
       . Political upheaval in the East Roman heartlands made efforts to retain control of these territories difficult and they were gradually lost, this time for good.
      </p>
      <p>
       Though the Eastern Empire retained territories in the south of Italy until the 11th century, the influence that the Empire had over
       <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">
        Western Europe
       </a>
       had diminished significantly with the
       <a href="/wiki/Pope" title="Pope">
        papal
       </a>
       coronation of the
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Frankish_kings" title="List of Frankish kings">
        Frankish king
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">
        Charlemagne
       </a>
       as "Roman Emperor" in 800 AD. His imperial line would come to evolve into the
       <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">
        Holy Roman Empire
       </a>
       , a revival of the imperial title in the West but in no meaningful sense an extension of Roman traditions or institutions. The
       <a href="/wiki/East%E2%80%93West_Schism" title="East–West Schism">
        Great Schism of 1054
       </a>
       between the churches of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bishop_of_rome" title="Bishop of rome">
        Rome
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Constantinople" title="Bishop of Constantinople">
        Constantinople
       </a>
       further diminshed the authority the Emperor in Constantinople could hope to bring forth in the west.
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

         </a>

      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Background">
        Background
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Western_Roman_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       As the
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">
        Roman Republic
       </a>
       expanded, it reached a point where the central government in
       <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">
        Rome
       </a>
       could not effectively rule the distant provinces. Communications and transportation were especially problematic given the vast extent of the Empire. News of invasion, revolt, natural disasters, or epidemic outbreak was carried by ship or
       <a href="/wiki/Cursus_publicus" title="Cursus publicus">
        mounted postal service
       </a>
       , often requiring much time to reach Rome and for Rome's orders to be realized in the province of origin. For this reason, provincial
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Governor" title="Roman Governor">
        governors
       </a>
       had
       <a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">
        de facto
       </a>
       rule in the name of the Roman Republic. Governors had several duties, including the command of armies, handling the taxes of the province and serving as a local chief judges.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Prior to the establishment of the Empire, the territories of the
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">
        Roman Republic
       </a>
       had been divided in 43 BC among the members of the
       <a href="/wiki/Second_Triumvirate" title="Second Triumvirate">
        Second Triumvirate
       </a>
       :
       <a href="/wiki/Mark_Antony" title="Mark Antony">
        Mark Antony
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Augustus" title="Augustus">
        Octavian
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Aemilius_Lepidus_(triumvir)" title="Marcus Aemilius Lepidus (triumvir)">
        Marcus Aemilius Lepidus
       </a>
       . Antony received the provinces in the East:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Achaea_Province" title="Achaea Province">
        Achaea
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_province_of_Macedonia" title="Roman province of Macedonia">
        Macedonia
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Epirus" title="Epirus">
        Epirus
       </a>
       (roughly modern
       <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">
        Greece
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">
        Albania
       </a>
       and the coast of
       <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">
        Croatia
       </a>
       ),
       <a href="/wiki/Bithynia" title="Bithynia">
        Bithynia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Pontus_(region)" title="Pontus (region)">
        Pontus
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Asia_(Roman_province)" title="Asia (Roman province)">
        Asia
       </a>
       (roughly modern
       <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">
        Turkey
       </a>
       ),
       <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">
        Syria
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">
        Cyprus
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Cyrenaica" title="Cyrenaica">
        Cyrenaica
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:9_3-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:9-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       These lands had previously been conquered by
       <a href="/wiki/Alexander_the_Great" title="Alexander the Great">
        Alexander the Great
       </a>
       ; thus, much of the
       <a href="/wiki/Aristocracy" title="Aristocracy">
        aristocracy
       </a>
       was of Greek origin. The whole region, especially the major cities, had been largely assimilated into Greek culture,
       <a href="/wiki/Koine_Greek" title="Koine Greek">
        Greek
       </a>
       often serving as the
       <a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">
        lingua franca
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Roman_Republic-44BC.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="624" data-file-width="1020" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Roman_Republic-44BC.png/250px-Roman_Republic-44BC.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Roman_Republic-44BC.png/375px-Roman_Republic-44BC.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Roman_Republic-44BC.png/500px-Roman_Republic-44BC.png 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Roman_Republic-44BC.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">
          Roman Republic
         </a>
         before the conquests of
         <a href="/wiki/Augustus" title="Augustus">
          Octavian
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Octavian obtained the Roman provinces of the West:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italia_(Roman_province)" title="Italia (Roman province)">
        Italia
       </a>
       (modern
       <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">
        Italy
       </a>
       ),
       <a href="/wiki/Gaul" title="Gaul">
        Gaul
       </a>
       (modern
       <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">
        France
       </a>
       ),
       <a href="/wiki/Gallia_Belgica" title="Gallia Belgica">
        Gallia Belgica
       </a>
       (parts of modern
       <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">
        Belgium
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">
        Netherlands
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">
        Luxembourg
       </a>
       ), and
       <a href="/wiki/Hispania" title="Hispania">
        Hispania
       </a>
       (modern
       <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
        Spain
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">
        Portugal
       </a>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:9_3-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:9-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       These lands also included Greek and Carthaginian colonies in the coastal areas, though
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Celt" title="Celt">
        Celtic
       </a>
       tribes such as
       <a href="/wiki/Gauls" title="Gauls">
        Gauls
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Celtiberians" title="Celtiberians">
        Celtiberians
       </a>
       were culturally dominant. Lepidus received the minor province of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Africa_Province" title="Africa Province">
        Africa
       </a>
       (roughly modern
       <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">
        Tunisia
       </a>
       ). Octavian soon took Africa from Lepidus, while adding
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sicilia_(province)" title="Sicilia (province)">
        Sicilia
       </a>
       (modern
       <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">
        Sicily
       </a>
       ) to his holdings.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Upon the defeat of Mark Antony, a victorious Octavian controlled a united
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">
        Roman Empire
       </a>
       . While the Roman Empire featured many distinct cultures, all were often said to experience gradual
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Romanization_(cultural)" title="Romanization (cultural)">
         Romanization
        </a>
       </i>
       . While the predominantly Greek culture of the East and the predominantly Latin culture of the West functioned effectively as an integrated whole, political and military developments would ultimately realign the Empire along those cultural and linguistic lines.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Rebellions.2C_uprisings.2C_and_political_developments">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Rebellions,_uprisings,_and_political_developments">
        Rebellions, uprisings, and political developments
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Western_Roman_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Rebellions, uprisings, and political developments">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Minor rebellions and uprisings were fairly common events throughout the Empire. Conquered tribes or cities would revolt, and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_legions" title="Roman legions">
        legions
       </a>
       would be detached to crush the rebellion. While this process was simple in peacetime, it could be considerably more complicated in wartime, as for example in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_Jewish-Roman_War" title="First Jewish-Roman War">
        Great Jewish Revolt
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In a full-blown
       <a href="/wiki/Military_campaign" title="Military campaign">
        military campaign
       </a>
       , the legions, under generals such as
       <a href="/wiki/Vespasian" title="Vespasian">
        Vespasian
       </a>
       , were far more numerous. To ensure a commander's loyalty, a pragmatic emperor might hold some members of the general's family
       <a href="/wiki/Hostage" title="Hostage">
        hostage
       </a>
       . To this end,
       <a href="/wiki/Nero" title="Nero">
        Nero
       </a>
       effectively held
       <a href="/wiki/Domitian" title="Domitian">
        Domitian
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Quintus_Petillius_Cerialis" title="Quintus Petillius Cerialis">
        Quintus Petillius Cerialis
       </a>
       , governor of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ostia_Antica_(archaeological_site)" title="Ostia Antica (archaeological site)">
        Ostia
       </a>
       , who were respectively the younger son and brother-in-law of Vespasian. The rule of Nero ended only with the revolt of the
       <a href="/wiki/Praetorian_Guard" title="Praetorian Guard">
        Praetorian Guard
       </a>
       , who had been bribed in the name of
       <a href="/wiki/Galba" title="Galba">
        Galba
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Praetorian_Guard" title="Praetorian Guard">
        Praetorian Guard
       </a>
       , a figurative "sword of
       <a href="/wiki/Damocles" title="Damocles">
        Damocles
       </a>
       ", were often perceived as being of dubious loyalty. Following their example, the legions at the borders increased participation in the
       <a href="/wiki/Civil_war" title="Civil war">
        civil wars
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The main enemy in the West was arguably the
       <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">
        Germanic tribes
       </a>
       behind the rivers
       <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">
        Rhine
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">
        Danube
       </a>
       . Augustus had tried to conquer them but ultimately pulled back after the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Teutoburg_Forest" title="Battle of the Teutoburg Forest">
        Teutoburg
       </a>
       reversal.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Parthian_Empire" title="Parthian Empire">
        Parthian Empire
       </a>
       , in the East, on the other hand, was too remote and powerful to be conquered. Any Parthian invasion was confronted and usually defeated; similarly, Parthians repelled some attempts of Roman invasion, however, even after successful wars of conquest, such as those implemented by
       <a href="/wiki/Trajan" title="Trajan">
        Trajan
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Septimius_Severus" title="Septimius Severus">
        Septimius Severus
       </a>
       . Those distant territories were forsaken to prevent unrest and also to ensure a more healthy and lasting peace with the Persians. The Parthians were followed by the
       <a href="/wiki/Sasanian_Empire" title="Sasanian Empire">
        Sasanian Empire
       </a>
       , which
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman-Sasanian_wars" title="Roman-Sasanian wars">
        continued hostilities
       </a>
       with the Roman Empire.
      </p>
      <p>
       Controlling the western border of Rome was reasonably easy because it was relatively close and also because of the disunity between the Germanic foes, however, controlling both frontiers altogether during wartime was difficult. If the emperor was near the border in the East, chances were high that an ambitious general would rebel in the West and vice versa. This wartime opportunism plagued many ruling emperors and indeed paved the road to power for several future emperors.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Crisis_of_the_Third_Century">
        Crisis of the Third Century
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Western_Roman_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Crisis of the Third Century">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Crisis_of_the_Third_Century" title="Crisis of the Third Century">
        Crisis of the Third Century
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Ancient_Rome_271_AD.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1213" data-file-width="2050" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Map_of_Ancient_Rome_271_AD.svg/250px-Map_of_Ancient_Rome_271_AD.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Map_of_Ancient_Rome_271_AD.svg/375px-Map_of_Ancient_Rome_271_AD.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Map_of_Ancient_Rome_271_AD.svg/500px-Map_of_Ancient_Rome_271_AD.svg.png 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Ancient_Rome_271_AD.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The Roman Empire in 268
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       With the assassination of the Emperor
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alexander_Severus" title="Alexander Severus">
        Alexander Severus
       </a>
       on 18 March 235, the Roman Empire sank into a 50-year civil war, now known as the
       <a href="/wiki/Crisis_of_the_Third_Century" title="Crisis of the Third Century">
        Crisis of the Third Century
       </a>
       . The rise of the bellicose
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sassanid_dynasty" title="Sassanid dynasty">
        Sassanid dynasty
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Parthia" title="Parthia">
        Parthia
       </a>
       posed a major threat to Rome in the east. Demonstrating the increased danger, Emperor
       <a href="/wiki/Valerian_(emperor)" title="Valerian (emperor)">
        Valerian
       </a>
       was captured by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shapur_I_of_Persia" title="Shapur I of Persia">
        Shapur I
       </a>
       in 259. His eldest son and heir-apparent,
       <a href="/wiki/Gallienus" title="Gallienus">
        Gallienus
       </a>
       , succeeded and took up the fight on the eastern frontier. Gallienus' son,
       <a href="/wiki/Saloninus" title="Saloninus">
        Saloninus
       </a>
       , and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Praetorian_Prefect" title="Praetorian Prefect">
        Praetorian Prefect
       </a>
       Silvanus were residing in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colonia_Agrippina" title="Colonia Agrippina">
        Colonia Agrippina
       </a>
       (modern
       <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">
        Cologne
       </a>
       ) to solidify the loyalty of the local legions. Nevertheless,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marcus_Cassianius_Latinius_Postumus" title="Marcus Cassianius Latinius Postumus">
        Marcus Cassianius Latinius Postumus
       </a>
       - the local governor of the German provinces — rebelled; his assault on Colonia Agrippina resulted in the deaths of Saloninus and the prefect. In the confusion that followed, an independent state known as the
       <a href="/wiki/Gallic_Empire" title="Gallic Empire">
        Gallic Empire
       </a>
       emerged.
      </p>
      <p>
       Its
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Capital_(political)" title="Capital (political)">
        capital
       </a>
       was Augusta Treverorum (modern
       <a href="/wiki/Trier" title="Trier">
        Trier
       </a>
       ), and it quickly expanded its control over the German and Gaulish provinces and over all of
       <a href="/wiki/Hispania" title="Hispania">
        Hispania
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Britain" title="Roman Britain">
        Britannia
       </a>
       . It had its own
       <a href="/wiki/Senate" title="Senate">
        senate
       </a>
       , and a partial list of its
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_consul" title="Roman consul">
        consuls
       </a>
       still survives. It maintained Roman religion, language, and culture, and was far more concerned with fighting the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Germanic_tribes" title="Germanic tribes">
        Germanic tribes
       </a>
       than other Romans. However, in the reign of
       <a href="/wiki/Claudius_Gothicus" title="Claudius Gothicus">
        Claudius Gothicus
       </a>
       (268 to 270), large expanses of the Gallic Empire were restored to Roman rule. At roughly the same time, several eastern provinces seceded under the
       <a href="/wiki/Palmyrene_Empire" title="Palmyrene Empire">
        Palmyrene Empire
       </a>
       , under the rule of Queen
       <a href="/wiki/Zenobia" title="Zenobia">
        Zenobia
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In 272, Emperor
       <a href="/wiki/Aurelian" title="Aurelian">
        Aurelian
       </a>
       finally managed to reclaim Palmyra and its territory for the empire. With the East secure, his attention was turned to the West, taking the Gallic Empire a year later. Because of a secret deal between Aurelian and Gallic Emperor
       <a href="/wiki/Tetricus_I" title="Tetricus I">
        Tetricus I
       </a>
       and his son
       <a href="/wiki/Tetricus_II" title="Tetricus II">
        Tetricus II
       </a>
       , the Gallic army was swiftly defeated. In exchange, Aurelian spared their lives and gave the two former rebels important positions in Italy.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Western_Roman_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: History">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tetrarchy">
        Tetrarchy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Western_Roman_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Tetrarchy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">

       <a href="/wiki/Tetrarchy" title="Tetrarchy">
        Tetrarchy
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Constantine_the_Great" title="Constantine the Great">
        Constantine the Great
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wars-of-the-Tetrarchy.gif">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="684" data-file-width="1000" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Wars-of-the-Tetrarchy.gif/230px-Wars-of-the-Tetrarchy.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Wars-of-the-Tetrarchy.gif/345px-Wars-of-the-Tetrarchy.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Wars-of-the-Tetrarchy.gif/460px-Wars-of-the-Tetrarchy.gif 2x" width="230"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wars-of-the-Tetrarchy.gif" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The organization of the Empire under the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tetrachy" title="Tetrachy">
          Tetrarchy
         </a>
         and its collapse due to
         <a href="/wiki/Constantine_the_Great" title="Constantine the Great">
          Constantine I
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The external borders were mostly stable for the remainder of the Crisis of the Third Century, although, between the death of Aurelian in 275 and the accession of Diocletian ten years later, at least eight emperors or would-be emperors were killed, many assassinated by their own troops.
      </p>
      <p>
       Under Diocletian, the political division of the Roman Empire began. In 285, he promoted
       <a href="/wiki/Maximian" title="Maximian">
        Maximian
       </a>
       to the rank of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Augustus_(title)" title="Augustus (title)">
        Augustus
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       (Emperor) and gave him control of the Western regions of the Empire. In 293,
       <a href="/wiki/Galerius" title="Galerius">
        Galerius
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Constantius_Chlorus" title="Constantius Chlorus">
        Constantius Chlorus
       </a>
       were appointed as their subordinates (
       <a href="/wiki/Caesar_(title)" title="Caesar (title)">
        Caesars
       </a>
       ), creating the First
       <a href="/wiki/Tetrarchy" title="Tetrarchy">
        Tetrarchy
       </a>
       . This system effectively divided the Empire into four major regions and created separate capitals besides Rome as a way to avoid the civil unrest that had marked the 3rd century. In the West, the capitals were Maximian's
       <a href="/wiki/Mediolanum" title="Mediolanum">
        Mediolanum
       </a>
       (now
       <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">
        Milan
       </a>
       ) and Constantius'
       <a href="/wiki/Trier" title="Trier">
        Trier
       </a>
       . In the East, the capitals were
       <a href="/wiki/Sirmium" title="Sirmium">
        Sirmium
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Nicomedia" title="Nicomedia">
        Nicomedia
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On 1 May 305, the two senior Augusti stepped down, and their respective Caesars were promoted to Augusti and appointed two new Caesars, thus creating the Second Tetrarchy.
      </p>
      <p>
       The system of the Tetrarchy quickly ran aground when the Western Roman Empire's Constantius died unexpectedly in 306, and his son
       <a href="/wiki/Constantine_the_Great" title="Constantine the Great">
        Constantine the Great
       </a>
       was proclaimed Augustus of the West by the legions in Britain.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A crisis followed as several claimants attempted to rule the Western half. In 308, the Augustus of the East,
       <a href="/wiki/Galerius" title="Galerius">
        Galerius
       </a>
       , arranged a conference at
       <a href="/wiki/Carnuntum" title="Carnuntum">
        Carnuntum
       </a>
       which revived the Tetrarchy by dividing the West between Constantine and a newcomer named
       <a href="/wiki/Licinius" title="Licinius">
        Licinius
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Constantine was far more interested in conquering the whole empire. Through a series of battles in the East and the West, Licinius and Constantine stabilized their respective parts of the Roman Empire by 314, and began to compete for sole control of a reunified state. Constantine emerged victorious in 324 after the surrender and murder of Licinius following the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Chrysopolis" title="Battle of Chrysopolis">
        Battle of Chrysopolis
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Following his victory and the unification of the Empire under one ruler once more, Constantine refounded the city of
       <a href="/wiki/Byzantium" title="Byzantium">
        Byzantium
       </a>
       in modern-day Greece as
       <i>
        Nova Roma
       </i>
       ("New Rome", later to be renamed
       <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">
        Constantinople
       </a>
       ) as the new capital of the Empire, shifting the administrative center of the Empire to the East.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Tetrarchy ended, but the idea of dividing the Roman Empire between two emperors had been validated. Very strong emperors would reunite it under their single rule, but with their death the Roman Empire would be divided again and again between the East and the West.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Further_divisions">
        Further divisions
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Western_Roman_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Further divisions">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Impero_Romano_da_maggio_a_settembre_337.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="474" data-file-width="688" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Impero_Romano_da_maggio_a_settembre_337.png/250px-Impero_Romano_da_maggio_a_settembre_337.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Impero_Romano_da_maggio_a_settembre_337.png/375px-Impero_Romano_da_maggio_a_settembre_337.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Impero_Romano_da_maggio_a_settembre_337.png/500px-Impero_Romano_da_maggio_a_settembre_337.png 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Impero_Romano_da_maggio_a_settembre_337.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Division of the Roman Empire among the Caesars appointed by
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Constantine_I" title="Constantine I">
          Constantine I
         </a>
         : from west to east, the territories of
         <a href="/wiki/Constantine_II_(emperor)" title="Constantine II (emperor)">
          Constantine II
         </a>
         ,
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Constans_I" title="Constans I">
          Constans I
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Dalmatius" title="Dalmatius">
          Dalmatius
         </a>
         and Constantius II. After the death of Constantine I (May 337), this was the formal division of the Empire, until Dalmatius was killed and his territory divided between Constans and Constantius.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Constantius_II" title="Constantius II">
        Constantius
       </a>
       was born in 317 at
       <a href="/wiki/Sirmium" title="Sirmium">
        Sirmium
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Pannonia" title="Pannonia">
        Pannonia
       </a>
       . He was the third son of
       <a href="/wiki/Constantine_the_Great" title="Constantine the Great">
        Constantine the Great
       </a>
       , and second by his second wife
       <a href="/wiki/Fausta" title="Fausta">
        Fausta
       </a>
       , the daughter of
       <a href="/wiki/Maximian" title="Maximian">
        Maximian
       </a>
       . Constantius was made
       <a href="/wiki/Caesar_(title)" title="Caesar (title)">
        Caesar
       </a>
       by his father on 13 November 324.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Roman Empire was under the rule of a single Emperor, but, with the death of Constantine in 337, the empire was partitioned between his surviving male heirs.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Constantius received the eastern provinces, including Constantinople,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Thrace" title="Roman Thrace">
        Thrace
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asia_Minor" title="Asia Minor">
        Asia Minor
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Syria" title="Roman Syria">
        Syria
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Egypt" title="Roman Egypt">
        Egypt
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Cyrenaica" title="Cyrenaica">
        Cyrenaica
       </a>
       ;
       <a href="/wiki/Constantine_II_(emperor)" title="Constantine II (emperor)">
        Constantine II
       </a>
       received
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Britain" title="Roman Britain">
        Britannia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Gaul" title="Roman Gaul">
        Gaul
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Hispania" title="Hispania">
        Hispania
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Mauretania_Tingitana" title="Mauretania Tingitana">
        Mauretania
       </a>
       ; and
       <a href="/wiki/Constans" title="Constans">
        Constans
       </a>
       , initially under the supervision of Constantine II, received
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italia_(Roman_Empire)" title="Italia (Roman Empire)">
        Italy
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Africa_Province" title="Africa Province">
        Africa
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Illyricum_(Roman_province)" title="Illyricum (Roman province)">
        Illyricum
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Pannonia" title="Pannonia">
        Pannonia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_(Roman_province)" title="Macedonia (Roman province)">
        Macedonia
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Achaea_(Roman_province)" title="Achaea (Roman province)">
        Achaea
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The provinces of Thrace, Achaea and Macedonia were shortly controlled by
       <a href="/wiki/Dalmatius" title="Dalmatius">
        Dalmatius
       </a>
       , nephew of Constantine I and a
       <i>
        caesar
       </i>
       and not an
       <i>
        Augustus
       </i>
       , until his murder by his own soldiers in 337.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The West was unified in 340 under Constans, who was assassinated in 350 under the order of the usurper
       <a href="/wiki/Magnentius" title="Magnentius">
        Magnentius
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       ; after Magnentius lost the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Mursa_Major" title="Battle of Mursa Major">
        Battle of Mursa Major
       </a>
       and committed suicide, a complete reunification of the whole Empire occurred in 353, with Constantius.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Constantius II focused most of his power in the East. Under his rule, the city of
       <a href="/wiki/Byzantium" title="Byzantium">
        Byzantium
       </a>
       - only recently re-founded as
       <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">
        Constantinople
       </a>
       - was fully developed as a capital. In 361, Constantius II became ill and died, and Constantius Chlorus' grandson
       <a href="/wiki/Julian_(emperor)" title="Julian (emperor)">
        Julian
       </a>
       , who had served as Constantius II's Caesar, assumed power. Julian was killed in 363 in the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Samarra" title="Battle of Samarra">
        Battle of Samarra
       </a>
       against the
       <a href="/wiki/Persian_Empire" title="Persian Empire">
        Persian Empire
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and was succeeded by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jovian_(Emperor)" title="Jovian (Emperor)">
        Jovian
       </a>
       , who ruled only until 364.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Theodosius_I%27s_empire.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="406" data-file-width="563" height="180" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Theodosius_I%27s_empire.png/250px-Theodosius_I%27s_empire.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Theodosius_I%27s_empire.png/375px-Theodosius_I%27s_empire.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Theodosius_I%27s_empire.png/500px-Theodosius_I%27s_empire.png 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Theodosius_I%27s_empire.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The division of the Empire after the death of Theodosius I, ca.395 AD superimposed on modern borders.
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #B53637; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          Western Court under
          <a href="/wiki/Honorius_(emperor)" title="Honorius (emperor)">
           Honorius
          </a>
         </div>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #8F36B5; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Roman_Empire" title="Eastern Roman Empire">
           Eastern Court
          </a>
          under
          <a href="/wiki/Arcadius" title="Arcadius">
           Arcadius
          </a>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Following the death of Jovian,
       <a href="/wiki/Valentinian_I" title="Valentinian I">
        Valentinian I
       </a>
       emerged as Emperor in 364. He immediately divided the Empire once again, giving the eastern half to his brother
       <a href="/wiki/Valens" title="Valens">
        Valens
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Stability was not achieved for long in either half, as the conflicts with outside forces (tribes) intensified. In 376, the
       <a href="/wiki/Visigoths" title="Visigoths">
        Visigoths
       </a>
       , fleeing before the
       <a href="/wiki/Ostrogoths" title="Ostrogoths">
        Ostrogoths
       </a>
       , who in turn were fleeing before the
       <a href="/wiki/Huns" title="Huns">
        Huns
       </a>
       , were allowed to cross the river Danube and settle into the Balkans by the Eastern government. Mistreatment caused a full-scale rebellion, and in 378 they inflicted a crippling defeat on the Eastern Roman field army in the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Adrianople" title="Battle of Adrianople">
        Battle of Adrianople
       </a>
       , in which Valens also died.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The campaigns to subdue them were only partly successful, and they officially became semi-independent
       <a href="/wiki/Foederati" title="Foederati">
        foederati
       </a>
       under their own leaders.
      </p>
      <p>
       More than in the East, there was also opposition to the Christianizing policy of the Emperors in the western half of the Empire. In 379,
       <a href="/wiki/Valentinian_I" title="Valentinian I">
        Valentinian I
       </a>
       's son and successor
       <a href="/wiki/Gratian" title="Gratian">
        Gratian
       </a>
       declined to wear the mantle of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pontifex_Maximus" title="Pontifex Maximus">
        Pontifex Maximus
       </a>
       , and in 382 he rescinded the rights of pagan priests and removed the
       <a href="/wiki/Altar_of_Victory" title="Altar of Victory">
        Altar of Victory
       </a>
       from the
       <a href="/wiki/Curia" title="Curia">
        Roman Curia
       </a>
       , a decision which caused dissatisfaction among the traditionally pagan aristocracy of Rome.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Theodosius_I" title="Theodosius I">
        Theodosius I
       </a>
       later decreed a ban on all religions except
       <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">
        Christianity
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The political situation was unstable. In 383, a powerful and popular general named
       <a href="/wiki/Magnus_Maximus" title="Magnus Maximus">
        Magnus Maximus
       </a>
       seized power in the West and forced Gratian's half-brother
       <a href="/wiki/Valentinian_II" title="Valentinian II">
        Valentinian II
       </a>
       to flee to the East for aid; in a destructive civil war, the Eastern Emperor
       <a href="/wiki/Theodosius_I" title="Theodosius I">
        Theodosius I
       </a>
       restored him to power.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 392, the
       <a href="/wiki/Franks" title="Franks">
        Frankish
       </a>
       and pagan
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Magister_militum" title="Magister militum">
         magister militum
        </a>
       </i>
       <a href="/wiki/Arbogast_(general)" title="Arbogast (general)">
        Arbogast
       </a>
       assassinated Valentinian II and proclaimed an obscure senator named
       <a href="/wiki/Eugenius" title="Eugenius">
        Eugenius
       </a>
       as Emperor. In 394 the forces of the two halves of the Empire again
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Frigidus" title="Battle of the Frigidus">
        clashed
       </a>
       with great loss of life. Again Theodosius I won, and he briefly ruled a united Empire until his death in 395. He was the last Emperor to rule both parts of the Roman Empire
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       ; his older son
       <a href="/wiki/Arcadius" title="Arcadius">
        Arcadius
       </a>
       inherited the eastern half while the younger
       <a href="/wiki/Honorius_(emperor)" title="Honorius (emperor)">
        Honorius
       </a>
       got the western half. Both were still minors and neither was capable of ruling effectively. Honorius was placed under the tutelage of the half-Roman/half-barbarian
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Magister_militum" title="Magister militum">
         magister militum
        </a>
       </i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flavius_Stilicho" title="Flavius Stilicho">
        Flavius Stilicho
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       while
       <a href="/wiki/Rufinus_(consul)" title="Rufinus (consul)">
        Rufinus
       </a>
       became the power behind the throne in the east. Rufinus and Stilicho were rivals, and their disagreements were exploited by the Gothic leader
       <a href="/wiki/Alaric_I" title="Alaric I">
        Alaric I
       </a>
       who again rebelled following the death of Theodosius I. Neither half of the Empire could raise forces sufficient even to subdue Alaric's men, and both tried to use Alaric against the other half.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Alaric himself tried to establish a long-term territorial and official base, but was never able to do so.
      </p>
      <p>
       Stilicho tried to defend Italy and bring the invading Goths under control, but to do so he stripped the Rhine frontier of troops and the
       <a href="/wiki/Vandals" title="Vandals">
        Vandals
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Alans" title="Alans">
        Alans
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suevi" title="Suevi">
        Suevi
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Crossing_of_the_Rhine" title="Crossing of the Rhine">
        invaded Gaul
       </a>
       in large numbers. Stilicho became a victim of court intrigues and was killed in 408. While the East began a slow recovery and consolidation, the West began to collapse entirely. Alaric's men
       <a href="/wiki/Sack_of_Rome_(410)" title="Sack of Rome (410)">
        sacked Rome
       </a>
       in 410.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Reign_of_Honorius">
        Reign of Honorius
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Western_Roman_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Reign of Honorius">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Honorius_(emperor)" title="Honorius (emperor)">
        Honorius (emperor)
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Solidus_of_Honorius_(YORYM_2001_12465_2)_obverse.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2076" data-file-width="2136" height="214" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Solidus_of_Honorius_%28YORYM_2001_12465_2%29_obverse.jpg/220px-Solidus_of_Honorius_%28YORYM_2001_12465_2%29_obverse.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Solidus_of_Honorius_%28YORYM_2001_12465_2%29_obverse.jpg/330px-Solidus_of_Honorius_%28YORYM_2001_12465_2%29_obverse.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Solidus_of_Honorius_%28YORYM_2001_12465_2%29_obverse.jpg/440px-Solidus_of_Honorius_%28YORYM_2001_12465_2%29_obverse.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Solidus_of_Honorius_(YORYM_2001_12465_2)_obverse.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Solidus of Emperor
         <a href="/wiki/Honorius_(emperor)" title="Honorius (emperor)">
          Honorius
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Honorius, the younger son of Theodosius I, was declared
       <i>
        Augustus
       </i>
       (and as such co-emperor with his father) on January 23rd in 393. Upon the death of Theodosius, Honorius inherited the throne of the West at the age of ten whilst his older brother
       <a href="/wiki/Arcadius" title="Arcadius">
        Arcadius
       </a>
       inherited the East.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
        <a href="#cite_note-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The western capital was initially
       <a href="/wiki/Mediolanum" title="Mediolanum">
        Mediolanum
       </a>
       , as it had been during previous divisions, but it was moved to
       <a href="/wiki/Ravenna" title="Ravenna">
        Ravenna
       </a>
       in 402 upon the entrance of the
       <a href="/wiki/Visigoths" title="Visigoths">
        visigothic
       </a>
       king
       <a href="/wiki/Alaric_I" title="Alaric I">
        Alaric I
       </a>
       into Italy. Ravenna, protected by abundant marshes and strong fortifactions, was far easier to defend but made it more difficult for the Roman military to defend central parts of Italy from the regular barbarian incursions.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Ravenna would remain the western capital until the deposition of
       <a href="/wiki/Romulus_Augustulus" title="Romulus Augustulus">
        Romulus Augustus
       </a>
       74 years later and would later be used as the capital for both the
       <a href="/wiki/Ostrogothic_Kingdom" title="Ostrogothic Kingdom">
        Ostrogothic Kingdom
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Exarchate_of_Ravenna" title="Exarchate of Ravenna">
        Exarchate of Ravenna
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The reign of Honorius was, even by Western Roman standards, chaotic and plagued by both internal and external struggles. The Visigothic
       <i>
        foederati
       </i>
       under Alaric,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Magister_militum" title="Magister militum">
         magister militum
        </a>
       </i>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Illyricum_(Roman_province)" title="Illyricum (Roman province)">
        Illyricum
       </a>
       , rebelled as early as 395.
       <a href="/wiki/Gildo" title="Gildo">
        Gildo
       </a>
       , the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Comes" title="Comes">
         Comes
        </a>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Africa_Province" title="Africa Province">
         Africae
        </a>
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        Magister utriusque militiae per Africam
       </i>
       , rebelled in 397 and initiated the
       <a href="/wiki/Gildonic_War" title="Gildonic War">
        Gildonic War
       </a>
       . Stilicho managed to subdue Gildo but was away in
       <a href="/wiki/Raetia" title="Raetia">
        Raetia
       </a>
       when the Visigoths entered Italy in 402.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
        <a href="#cite_note-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Stilicho, hurrying back to aid in defending Italy, summoned legions in Gaul and Britain with which he managed to defeat Alaric twice before agreeing to allow him to retreat back to Illyria.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Western_Roman_Empire_409.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3323" data-file-width="3500" height="209" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Western_Roman_Empire_409.png/220px-Western_Roman_Empire_409.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Western_Roman_Empire_409.png/330px-Western_Roman_Empire_409.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Western_Roman_Empire_409.png/440px-Western_Roman_Empire_409.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Western_Roman_Empire_409.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Barbarian invasions and the invasion of usurper
         <a href="/wiki/Constantine_III_(Western_Roman_Emperor)" title="Constantine III (Western Roman Emperor)">
          Constantine III
         </a>
         in the Western Roman Empire during the reign of Honorius 407-409.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The weakened frontiers in Britain and Gaul had dire consequences for the empire. Numerous usurpers rose from Britain, including
       <a href="/wiki/Marcus_(usurper)" title="Marcus (usurper)">
        Marcus
       </a>
       (406–407),
       <a href="/wiki/Gratian_(usurper)" title="Gratian (usurper)">
        Gratian
       </a>
       (407), and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Constantine_III_(usurper)" title="Constantine III (usurper)">
        Constantine III
       </a>
       who invaded Gaul in 407. Britain was effectively abandoned by the empire by 410 due to the crumbling resources and the need to look after more important frontiers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_31-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:0-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The weakened rhine frontier allowed multiple barbarian tribes, including the
       <a href="/wiki/Vandals" title="Vandals">
        Vandals
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Alans" title="Alans">
        Alans
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Suebi" title="Suebi">
        Suebi
       </a>
       , to
       <a href="/wiki/Crossing_of_the_Rhine" title="Crossing of the Rhine">
        cross the river
       </a>
       and enter Roman territory in 406.
      </p>
      <p>
       Honorius was convinced by the minister
       <a href="/wiki/Olympius" title="Olympius">
        Olympius
       </a>
       that Stilicho was conspiring to overthrow him, and thus arrested and executed Stilicho in 408.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Olympius headed a conspiracy that successfully orchestrated the deaths of key individuals related to the regime of Stilicho, including his son and the families of many of his federated troops.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_31-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:0-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This lead many of the soldiers to instead join with Alaric, who returned to Italy in 409 and met little opposition. Despite attempts by Honorius to a settlement and six legions of Eastern Roman soldiers sent to support him
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nor2_33-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Nor2-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , the negotiations between Alaric and Honorius broke down in 410 and Alaric
       <a href="/wiki/Sack_of_Rome_(410)" title="Sack of Rome (410)">
        sacked the city of Rome
       </a>
       . Though the sack was relatively mild and Rome was no longer the capital, this event made a great impression on contemporaries, as this was the first time since the Gallic invasions of the 4th century BC that the city had fallen to a foreign enemy.
      </p>
      <p>
       Without Stilicho and following the sack of Rome, Honorius reign grew more and more chaotic. The usurper
       <a href="/wiki/Constantine_III_(Western_Roman_Emperor)" title="Constantine III (Western Roman Emperor)">
        Constantine III
       </a>
       had stripped Roman Britain of its defenses when he crossed over to Gaul in 407, leaving the Romanized population subject to invasions, first by the
       <a href="/wiki/Picts" title="Picts">
        Picts
       </a>
       and then by the
       <a href="/wiki/Saxons" title="Saxons">
        Saxons
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Angli" title="Angli">
        Angli
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/Jutes" title="Jutes">
        Jutes
       </a>
       who began to settle permanently from about 440 onwards. After Honorius accepted Constantine as co-emperor, Constantine's general in Hispania,
       <a href="/wiki/Gerontius_(general)" title="Gerontius (general)">
        Gerontius
       </a>
       , proclaimed
       <a href="/wiki/Maximus_of_Hispania" title="Maximus of Hispania">
        Maximus
       </a>
       as Emperor. With the aid of general
       <a href="/wiki/Constantius_III" title="Constantius III">
        Constantius
       </a>
       , Honorius successfully defeated Gerontius and Maximus in 411 and shortly thereafter captured and executed Constantine III. With Constantius back in Italy, the Gallo-Roman senator
       <a href="/wiki/Jovinus" title="Jovinus">
        Jovinus
       </a>
       revolted after proclaiming himself Emperor. With the support of the Gallic nobility and the barbarian
       <a href="/wiki/Burgundians" title="Burgundians">
        Burgundians
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Alans" title="Alans">
        Alans
       </a>
       , Honorius turned to the Visigoths under King
       <a href="/wiki/Ataulf" title="Ataulf">
        Ataulf
       </a>
       for support against Jovinus.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Ataulf defeated and executed Jovinus and his proclaimed co-emperor
       <a href="/wiki/Sebastianus" title="Sebastianus">
        Sebastianus
       </a>
       in 413, around the same time as another usurper rose in
       <a href="/wiki/Africa_(Roman_province)" title="Africa (Roman province)">
        Africa
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Heraclianus" title="Heraclianus">
        Heraclianus
       </a>
       . Heraclianus attempted to invade Italy but failed and retreated to Carthage, where he was killed.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       With the Roman legions withdrawn, northern Gaul became subject to more and more
       <a href="/wiki/Franks" title="Franks">
        Frankish
       </a>
       influence, the Franks naturally adopting a somewhat leading role in the region. In 418, Honorius granted southwestern Gaul (
       <a href="/wiki/Gallia_Aquitania" title="Gallia Aquitania">
        Gallia Aquitania
       </a>
       ) to the Visigoths as a vassal federation. Removing the local imperial governors, the Visigoths and the provincial Roman inhabitants were left to conduct their own affairs. As such, the first of the "
       <a href="/wiki/Barbarian_kingdoms" title="Barbarian kingdoms">
        barbarian kingdoms
       </a>
       ", the
       <a href="/wiki/Visigothic_Kingdom" title="Visigothic Kingdom">
        Visigothic Kingdom
       </a>
       , was formed.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:6_36-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:6-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Escalating_barbarian_conflicts">
        Escalating barbarian conflicts
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Western_Roman_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Escalating barbarian conflicts">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Invasions_of_the_Roman_Empire_1.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1362" data-file-width="1954" height="174" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Invasions_of_the_Roman_Empire_1.png/250px-Invasions_of_the_Roman_Empire_1.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Invasions_of_the_Roman_Empire_1.png/375px-Invasions_of_the_Roman_Empire_1.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Invasions_of_the_Roman_Empire_1.png/500px-Invasions_of_the_Roman_Empire_1.png 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Invasions_of_the_Roman_Empire_1.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Germanic and Hunnic invasions of the Roman Empire, 100–500 AD
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Honorius' death in 423 was followed by turmoil until the Eastern Roman government with the force of arms installed
       <a href="/wiki/Valentinian_III" title="Valentinian III">
        Valentinian III
       </a>
       as Western Emperor in Ravenna, with
       <a href="/wiki/Galla_Placidia" title="Galla Placidia">
        Galla Placidia
       </a>
       acting as regent during her son's minority. Theodosius II, Eastern Emperor, had hesitated to announce the death of Honorius and in the ensuing interregnum,
       <a href="/wiki/Joannes" title="Joannes">
        Joannes
       </a>
       was nominated as Western Emperor. Joannes "rule" was short and the forces of the East successfully defeated and executed him in 425.
      </p>
      <p>
       After a violent struggle with several rivals, and against Placidia's wish,
       <a href="/wiki/Flavius_Aetius" title="Flavius Aetius">
        Aetius
       </a>
       rose to the rank of
       <i>
        magister militum
       </i>
       . Aetius was able to stabilize the Western Empire's military situation somewhat, relying heavily on his
       <a href="/wiki/Huns#Unified_Empire_under_Attila" title="Huns">
        Hunnic
       </a>
       allies. With their help Aetius undertook extensive campaigns in Gaul, defeating the Visigoths in 437 and 438 but suffering a defeat himself in 439, ending the conflicts in a
       <i>
        status quo
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Meanwhile, pressure from the Visigoths and a rebellion by
       <a href="/wiki/Bonifacius" title="Bonifacius">
        Bonifacius
       </a>
       , the governor of Africa, induced the Vandals under their king
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gaiseric" title="Gaiseric">
        Gaiseric
       </a>
       to cross over from Spain in 429. They temporarily halted in Numidia (435) before moving eastward. With Aetius occupied in Gaul, the Western Roman government could do nothing to prevent the
       <a href="/wiki/Vandals" title="Vandals">
        Vandals
       </a>
       conquering the wealthy African provinces, eventually culminating in the fall of
       <a href="/wiki/Carthage" title="Carthage">
        Carthage
       </a>
       on 19 October 439 and the establishment of the
       <a href="/wiki/Vandal_Kingdom" title="Vandal Kingdom">
        Vandalic Kingdom
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_37-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:1-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       By the 400s, Italy and Rome itself was dependent on the taxes and foodstuffs from these provinces, leading to an economical crisis. With Vandal fleets becoming an increasingly constant danger to Roman sea trade and the coasts and islands of the western and central Mediterranean, Aetius coordinated a counterattack against the Vandals in 440, organizing a large army in Sicily.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_37-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:1-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       However, the plans of retaking Africa had to be abandoned due to the immediate need to combat the invading Huns, who in 444 were united under their ambitious king
       <a href="/wiki/Attila" title="Attila">
        Attila
       </a>
       . Turning against their former ally, the Huns became a formidable threat to the Empire. Aetius transferred his forces to the
       <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">
        Danube
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_37-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-:1-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , though Attila had begun to concentrate on raiding the Eastern Roman provinces in the Balkans, providing momentary relief to the Western court. In 449, Attila received a message from
       <a href="/wiki/Justa_Grata_Honoria" title="Justa Grata Honoria">
        Honoria
       </a>
       , Valentinian III’s sister, offering him half the western empire if he would rescue her from an unwanted marriage that her brother was forcing her into. With a pretext to invade the West, Attila secured peace with the Eastern court and crossed the
       <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">
        Rhine
       </a>
       in early 451.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
        <a href="#cite_note-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       With Attila wreaking havoc in Gaul, Aetius gathered together a coalition of Roman and Germanic forces, including Visigoths and Burgundians, and prevented the Huns from taking the city
       <a href="/wiki/Orl%C3%A9ans" title="Orléans">
        Aurelianum
       </a>
       , forcing them into retreat.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       At the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ch%C3%A2lons" title="Battle of Châlons">
        Battle of Châlons
       </a>
       , the Roman-Germanic coalition met and defeat the Hunnic forces, though Attila escaped.
      </p>
      <p>
       Attila regrouped and invaded Italy in 452. With Aetius not having enough forces to attack, the road to Rome was open. Valentinian sent
       <a href="/wiki/Pope_Leo_I" title="Pope Leo I">
        Pope Leo I
       </a>
       and two leading senators to negotiate with Attila. This embassy, combined with a plague among Attila's troops, the threat of famine, and news that the Eastern Emperor
       <a href="/wiki/Marcian" title="Marcian">
        Marcian
       </a>
       had launched an attack on Hun homelands along the Danube, forced Attila to turn around and leave Italy.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_40-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:2-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       With Attila dying unexpectedly in 453, the power struggle that erupted between his sons ended the threat posed by the Huns.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_40-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:2-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Internal_unrest_and_Majorian">
        Internal unrest and Majorian
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Western_Roman_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Internal unrest and Majorian">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Roman_Empire_under_Majorian_(460_CE).png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1385" data-file-width="1220" height="250" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Roman_Empire_under_Majorian_%28460_CE%29.png/220px-Roman_Empire_under_Majorian_%28460_CE%29.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Roman_Empire_under_Majorian_%28460_CE%29.png/330px-Roman_Empire_under_Majorian_%28460_CE%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Roman_Empire_under_Majorian_%28460_CE%29.png/440px-Roman_Empire_under_Majorian_%28460_CE%29.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Roman_Empire_under_Majorian_(460_CE).png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The Western Roman Empire during the reign of
         <a href="/wiki/Majorian" title="Majorian">
          Majorian
         </a>
         in 460 AD. During his four-year long reign from 457 to 461, Majorian successfully restored Western Roman authority in Hispania and most of Gaul. Despite his accomplishments, Roman rule in the west would last less than two more decades.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Valentinian III, feeling intimidated by Aetius, was enlisted by the Roman senator
       <a href="/wiki/Petronius_Maximus" title="Petronius Maximus">
        Petronius Maximus
       </a>
       and the chamberlain Heraclius to assassinate him. When Aetius was at court in Ravenna delivering a financial account, Valentinian suddenly leaped from his seat and declared that he would no longer be the victim of Aetius's drunken depravities. He held Aetius responsible for the empire's troubles and accused him of trying to steal the empire from him. Aetius attempted to defend himself from the charges, but Valentinian drew his sword and struck the weaponless Aetius on the head, killing him on the spot.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
        <a href="#cite_note-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On March 16 the following year, Valentinian himself was killed by supporters of the dead general, possibly put up to it by Petronius Maximus. With the end of the
       <a href="/wiki/Theodosian_dynasty" title="Theodosian dynasty">
        Theodosian dynasty
       </a>
       , Petronius Maximus proclaimed himself emperor during the ensuing period of unrest.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
        <a href="#cite_note-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Petronius was not prepared to take control over the significantly weaken and unstable Empire. Petronius broke the betrothal between Huneric, son of the
       <a href="/wiki/Vandal_Kingdom" title="Vandal Kingdom">
        Vandal
       </a>
       king
       <a href="/wiki/Genseric" title="Genseric">
        Gaiseric
       </a>
       , and Eudocia, daughter of Valentinian III. This was seen as just cause of war by King Gaiseric, who set sail to attack Rome. Petronius and his supporters attempted to flee the city at the sight of the approaching Vandals, only to be stoned to death by a Roman mob after a reign of only 11 weeks.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
        <a href="#cite_note-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
       With the Vandals at the gates, Pope Leo I requested that the king not destroy the ancient city or murder its inhabitants, to which Gaiseric agreed and the city gates were opened to him. Though keeping his promise, Gaiseric looted great amounts of treasure and damaged objects of cultural significance such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Temple_of_Jupiter_Optimus_Maximus" title="Temple of Jupiter Optimus Maximus">
        Temple of Jupiter Optimus Maximus
       </a>
       . The severity of the
       <a href="/wiki/Sack_of_Rome_(455)" title="Sack of Rome (455)">
        Vandal sack of 455
       </a>
       is disputed, though with the Vandals plundering the city for a full fourteen days as opposed to the
       <a href="/wiki/Sack_of_Rome_(410)" title="Sack of Rome (410)">
        Visigothic sack of 410
       </a>
       , where the Visigoths only spent three days in the city, it was likely more thorough.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Avitus" title="Avitus">
        Avitus
       </a>
