       , a prominent general under Petronius, was proclaimed emperor by the Visigothic king
       <a href="/wiki/Theodoric_II" title="Theodoric II">
        Theoderic II
       </a>
       and accepted as such by the
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Senate" title="Roman Senate">
        Roman senate
       </a>
       . Though supported by the Gallic provinces and the Visigoths, Avitus was resented in Italy due to ongoing food shortages caused by Vandal control of trade routes and for using a Visigothic imperial guard.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
        <a href="#cite_note-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Disbanding his guard due to popular pressure, the
       <a href="/wiki/Suebi" title="Suebi">
        Suebian
       </a>
       general
       <a href="/wiki/Ricimer" title="Ricimer">
        Ricimer
       </a>
       used this opportunity to depose Avitus, counting on popular discontent. After the deposition of Avitus, the Eastern Emperor
       <a href="/wiki/Leo_I_the_Thracian" title="Leo I the Thracian">
        Leo I
       </a>
       did not select a new western
       <i>
        Augustus
       </i>
       . After the prominent general
       <a href="/wiki/Majorian" title="Majorian">
        Majorian
       </a>
       defeated an invading force of
       <a href="/wiki/Alemanni" title="Alemanni">
        Alemanni
       </a>
       , he was proclaimed Western Emperor by the army
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
        <a href="#cite_note-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and eventually accepted as such by Eastern Emperor Leo I.
      </p>
      <p>
       Majorian was the last Western Emperor to attempt to recover the Western Empire with its own military forces. To prepare, Majorian significantly strengthened the Western Roman army by recruiting large numbers of barbarian mercenaries, among them m
       <a href="/wiki/Gepids" title="Gepids">
        Gepids
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ostrogoths" title="Ostrogoths">
        Ostrogoths
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Rugii" title="Rugii">
        Rugii
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Burgundians" title="Burgundians">
        Burgundians
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Huns" title="Huns">
        Huns
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Bastarnae" title="Bastarnae">
        Bastarnae
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Suebi" title="Suebi">
        Suebi
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Scythians" title="Scythians">
        Scythians
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Alans" title="Alans">
        Alans
       </a>
       , and built two fleets, one at Ravenna, to combat the strong
       <a href="/wiki/Vandal_Kingdom" title="Vandal Kingdom">
        vandalic
       </a>
       fleet.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
        <a href="#cite_note-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Majorian personally lead the army to wage war in Gaul, leaving Ricimer in Italy. The Gallic provinces and the
       <a href="/wiki/Visigothic_Kingdom" title="Visigothic Kingdom">
        Visigothic Kingdom
       </a>
       had rebelled following the deposition of Avitus, refusing to acknowledge Majorian as lawful emperor. At the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Arelate" title="Battle of Arelate">
        Battle of Arelate
       </a>
       , Majorian decisively defeated the Visigoths under
       <a href="/wiki/Theodoric_II" title="Theodoric II">
        Theoderic II
       </a>
       and forced them to relinquish their great conquests in
       <a href="/wiki/Hispania" title="Hispania">
        Hispania
       </a>
       and return to
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Foederati" title="Foederati">
         foederati
        </a>
       </i>
       status.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
        <a href="#cite_note-48">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Majorian then entered the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rhone_Valley" title="Rhone Valley">
        Rhone Valley
       </a>
       , where he defeated the Burgundians and reconquered the rebel city of Lugdunum.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
        <a href="#cite_note-49">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       With Gaul back under Roman control, Majorian turned his eyes to the Vandals and Africa. Not only did the Vandals pose a constant danger to coastal Italy and trade in the Mediterranean, but the province they ruled was economically vital to the survival of the West. Majorian began a campaign to fully reconquer Hispania to use it as a base of his conquest of Africa. Throughout 459, Majorian campaigned against the Suebi in northwestern Hispania.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Vandals began to increasingly fear a Roman invasion. King
       <a href="/wiki/Genseric" title="Genseric">
        Gaiseric
       </a>
       tried to negotiate a peace with Majorian, who rejected the proposal. In the wake of this, Gaiseric devastated
       <a href="/wiki/Mauretania_Caesariensis" title="Mauretania Caesariensis">
        Mauretania
       </a>
       , part of his own kingdom, fearing that the Roman army would land there. Having restored control of Hispania, Majorian intended to use his fleet at
       <a href="/wiki/Hispania_Carthaginensis" title="Hispania Carthaginensis">
        Carthaginiensis
       </a>
       to attack the Vandals. Before he could, the fleet was destroyed, allegedly by traitors paid by the Vandals.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
        <a href="#cite_note-50">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Deprived of his fleet, Majorian had to cancel his attack on the Vandals and conclude a peace with Gaiseric.
      </p>
      <p>
       Disbanding his barbarian forces, Majorian intended to return to Rome and issue reforms, stopping at
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arelate" title="Arelate">
        Arelate
       </a>
       on his way. Here, Ricimer deposed and arrested him in 461, having gathered significant aristocratical opposition against Majorian.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
        <a href="#cite_note-51">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
       After five days of beatings and torture, Majorian was beheaded near the river
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iria_(river)" title="Iria (river)">
        Iria
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
        <a href="#cite_note-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Collapse">
        Collapse
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Western_Roman_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Collapse">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_the_Western_Roman_Empire" title="Fall of the Western Roman Empire">
        Fall of the Western Roman Empire
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:251px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:628px-Western_and_Eastern_Roman_Empires_476AD(3).PNG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="259" data-file-width="528" height="122" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/628px-Western_and_Eastern_Roman_Empires_476AD%283%29.PNG/249px-628px-Western_and_Eastern_Roman_Empires_476AD%283%29.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/628px-Western_and_Eastern_Roman_Empires_476AD%283%29.PNG/374px-628px-Western_and_Eastern_Roman_Empires_476AD%283%29.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/628px-Western_and_Eastern_Roman_Empires_476AD%283%29.PNG/498px-628px-Western_and_Eastern_Roman_Empires_476AD%283%29.PNG 2x" width="249"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:628px-Western_and_Eastern_Roman_Empires_476AD(3).PNG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The Western and
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Roman_empire" title="Eastern Roman empire">
          Eastern Roman Empire
         </a>
         by 476.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The final collapse of the Empire in the West was marked by increasingly ineffectual puppet Emperors dominated by their Germanic
       <a href="/wiki/Magister_militum" title="Magister militum">
        masters of the soldiers
       </a>
       . The most pointed example of this is
       <a href="/wiki/Ricimer" title="Ricimer">
        Ricimer
       </a>
       , who effectively became a "Shadow Emperor" following the depositions of
       <a href="/wiki/Avitus" title="Avitus">
        Avitus
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Majorian" title="Majorian">
        Majorian
       </a>
       . Unable to take the throne for himself due to his barbarian heritage, Ricimer appointed a series of "puppet emperors" that could do little to halt the collapse of Roman authority and the loss of the territories reconquered by Majorian. The first of these puppet emperors,
       <a href="/wiki/Libius_Severus" title="Libius Severus">
        Libius Severus
       </a>
       , had no recognition outside of Italy, with the Eastern Emperor Leo I and provincial governors in Gaul and Illyria all refusing to recognize him. Severus died in 465 and Leo I, with the consent of Ricimer, appointed the capable Eastern general
       <a href="/wiki/Anthemius" title="Anthemius">
        Anthemius
       </a>
       as Western Emperor following an eighteen-month Western
       <a href="/wiki/Interregnum" title="Interregnum">
        interregnum
       </a>
       . The relationship between Anthemius and the East was good, Anthemius is the last Western Emperor recorded in an Eastern law
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
        <a href="#cite_note-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , and the two courts conducted a joint operation to retake Africa from the Vandals, culminating in the disastrous
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cap_Bon_(468)" title="Battle of Cap Bon (468)">
        Battle of Cap Bon
       </a>
       in 468. Furthermore, Anthemius conducted failed campaigns against the Visigoths, hoping to halt their increasing expansion.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
        <a href="#cite_note-54">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The trial and subsequent execution of
       <a href="/wiki/Romanus_(usurper)" title="Romanus (usurper)">
        Romanus
       </a>
       , an Italian senator and friend of Ricimer, on the grounds of treachery in 470 made Ricimer hostile to Anthemius. Following two years of hostilities, Ricimer successfully deposed and killed Anthemius in 472, elevating
       <a href="/wiki/Olybrius" title="Olybrius">
        Olybrius
       </a>
       to the Western throne.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
        <a href="#cite_note-55">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
       During the brief reign of Olybrius, Ricimer died and his nephew
       <a href="/wiki/Gundobad" title="Gundobad">
        Gundobad
       </a>
       succeeded him as
       <i>
        magister militum
       </i>
       . After only seven months of rule, Olybrius died of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dropsy" title="Dropsy">
        dropsy
       </a>
       . Gundobad elevated
       <a href="/wiki/Glycerius" title="Glycerius">
        Glycerius
       </a>
       to Western Emperor. The Eastern Empire had rejected Olybrius and also rejected Glycerius, instead supporting a candidate of their own,
       <a href="/wiki/Julius_Nepos" title="Julius Nepos">
        Julius Nepos
       </a>
       ,
       <i>
        magister militum
       </i>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Dalmatia" title="Dalmatia">
        Dalmatia
       </a>
       . With the support of Eastern Emperors
       <a href="/wiki/Leo_II_(emperor)" title="Leo II (emperor)">
        Leo II
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Zeno_(emperor)" title="Zeno (emperor)">
        Zeno
       </a>
       , Julius Nepos crossed the
       <a href="/wiki/Adriatic_Sea" title="Adriatic Sea">
        Adriatic Sea
       </a>
       in the spring of 474 to depose Glycerius.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_56-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:3-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
       At the arrival of Nepos in Italy, Glycerius abdicated without a fight and was allowed to live out his life as the
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Split-Makarska" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Split-Makarska">
        Bishop of Salona
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_56-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:3-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The brief rule of Nepos in Italy ended in 475 when
       <a href="/wiki/Orestes_(father_of_Romulus_Augustulus)" title="Orestes (father of Romulus Augustulus)">
        Orestes
       </a>
       , a former secretary of
       <a href="/wiki/Attila" title="Attila">
        Attila
       </a>
       and the
       <i>
        magister militum
       </i>
       of Julius Nepos, took control of Ravenna and forced Nepos to flee by ship to Dalmatia. Later in the same year, Orestes crowned his own young son as Western Emperor under the name Romulus Augustus. Romulus Augustus was not recognised as Western Emperor by the Eastern Court, who maintained that Nepos was the only legal Western Emperor, reigning in exile from Dalmatia.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
        <a href="#cite_note-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On September 4, 476,
       <a href="/wiki/Odoacer" title="Odoacer">
        Odoacer
       </a>
       , leader of the Germanic
       <i>
        foederati
       </i>
       in Italy, captured Ravenna, killed Orestes and deposed Romulus. Though Romulus was deposed, Nepos did not return to Italy and continued to reign as Western Emperor from Dalmatia, with support from Constantinople. Odoacer proclaimed himself ruler of Italy and began to negotiate with the Eastern Emperor
       <a href="/wiki/Zeno_(emperor)" title="Zeno (emperor)">
        Zeno
       </a>
       . Zeno eventually granted Odoacer
       <a href="/wiki/Patrician_(ancient_Rome)" title="Patrician (ancient Rome)">
        patrician
       </a>
       status as recognition of his authority and accepted him as his own viceroy of Italy. Zeno, however, insisted that Odoacer had to pay homage to Julius Nepos as the Emperor of the Western Empire. Odoacer accepted this condition and issued coins in the name of Julius Nepos throughout Italy. This, however, was mainly an empty political gesture, as Odoacer never returned any real power or territories to Julius Nepos. The murder of Julius Nepos in 480 prompted Odoacer to invade Dalmatia, annexing it to his
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy_(476%E2%80%93493)" title="Kingdom of Italy (476–493)">
        Kingdom of Italy
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Last_Emperor">
        Last Emperor
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Western_Roman_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Last Emperor">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       By convention, the Western Roman Empire is deemed to have ended on 4 September 476, when
       <a href="/wiki/Odoacer" title="Odoacer">
        Odoacer
       </a>
       deposed
       <a href="/wiki/Romulus_Augustulus" title="Romulus Augustulus">
        Romulus Augustus
       </a>
       , but the historical record calls this determination into question.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_58-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:4-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Julius_Nepos" title="Julius Nepos">
        Julius Nepos
       </a>
       still claimed to be Emperor of the West, and ruled a
       <a href="/wiki/Rump_state" title="Rump state">
        rump state
       </a>
       in Dalmatia. He was recognized as such by Eastern Roman Emperor
       <a href="/wiki/Zeno_(emperor)" title="Zeno (emperor)">
        Zeno
       </a>
       and by
       <a href="/wiki/Syagrius" title="Syagrius">
        Syagrius
       </a>
       , who had managed to preserve Roman sovereignty in an
       <a href="/wiki/Enclave_and_exclave" title="Enclave and exclave">
        exclave
       </a>
       in northern Gaul, known today as the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Domain_of_Soissons" title="Domain of Soissons">
        Domain of Soissons
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:8_59-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:8-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Recognising that no direct Roman control remained over the territories legally governed by the western emperor, Zeno did not appoint a new western emperor after the death of Julius Nepos in 480. Instead Zeno abolished the juridical division of the position of emperor into two separate courts, declaring himself the sole emperor of a reunited Roman Empire. As such, the (eastern)
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Byzantine_emperors" title="List of Byzantine emperors">
        Roman emperors
       </a>
       after 480 are the successors of the western ones, albeit only in a juridical sense.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:11_60-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:11-60">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
       These emperors would continue to rule the Roman Empire until the
       <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_Constantinople" title="Fall of Constantinople">
        Fall of Constantinople
       </a>
       in 1453, nearly a thousand years later.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
        <a href="#cite_note-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Political_aftermath">
        Political aftermath
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Western_Roman_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Political aftermath">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Roman-Empire_477ad.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="954" data-file-width="1405" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Roman-Empire_477ad.jpg/250px-Roman-Empire_477ad.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Roman-Empire_477ad.jpg/375px-Roman-Empire_477ad.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Roman-Empire_477ad.jpg/500px-Roman-Empire_477ad.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Roman-Empire_477ad.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">
          Europe
         </a>
         in 477 AD. Highlighted areas are Roman lands that survived the deposition of
         <a href="/wiki/Romulus_Augustulus" title="Romulus Augustulus">
          Romulus Augustulus
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The deposition of
       <a href="/wiki/Romulus_Augustulus" title="Romulus Augustulus">
        Romulus Augustus
       </a>
       and the end of direct Roman rule in Italy in 476, often cited as the end of the Western Roman Empire, was evidently not seen as a world-changing event at the time. The Western court had lacked true power and been subject to Germanic aristocrats for decades, with most of its legal territory being under control of various
       <a href="/wiki/Barbarian_kingdoms" title="Barbarian kingdoms">
        barbarian kingdoms
       </a>
       . With Odoacer recognising
       <a href="/wiki/Julius_Nepos" title="Julius Nepos">
        Julius Nepos
       </a>
       , and later
       <a href="/wiki/Zeno_(emperor)" title="Zeno (emperor)">
        Zeno
       </a>
       , as his sovereign, nominal Roman control continued in Italy.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_58-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:4-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Some further territories of Roman control continued to exist in the West in some form even after 480. The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Domain_of_Soissons" title="Domain of Soissons">
        Domain of Soissons
       </a>
       , a rump state in Northern Gaul ruled by
       <a href="/wiki/Syagrius" title="Syagrius">
        Syagrius
       </a>
       , survived until 486 when it was conquered by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frankish_kingdom" title="Frankish kingdom">
        Franks
       </a>
       under King
       <a href="/wiki/Clovis_I" title="Clovis I">
        Clovis I
       </a>
       after the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Soissons_(486)" title="Battle of Soissons (486)">
        Battle of Soissons
       </a>
       . Syagrius was known as the "King of the Romans" by the Germanic peoples of the region and continually claimed that he was merely governing a Roman province, not an independent realm.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:8_59-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:8-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Furthermore, a Roman-Moor realm survived in the province of
       <a href="/wiki/Mauretania_Caesariensis" title="Mauretania Caesariensis">
        Mauretania Caesariensis
       </a>
       until the early 8th century. An inscription on a fortification at the ruined city of Altava from the year 508 identifies a man named
       <a href="/wiki/Masuna" title="Masuna">
        Masuna
       </a>
       as the king of "
       <i>
        Regnum Maurorum et Romanarum
       </i>
       ", the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mauro-Roman_kingdom" title="Mauro-Roman kingdom">
        Kingdom of the Moors and Romans
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
        <a href="#cite_note-62">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is possible that Masuna is the same man as the "Massonas" who allied himself with the forces of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Roman_empire" title="Eastern Roman empire">
        Eastern Roman Empire
       </a>
       against the
       <a href="/wiki/Vandals" title="Vandals">
        Vandals
       </a>
       in 535.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
        <a href="#cite_note-63">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As the Mauro-Roman realm shrank it eventually became known as the "
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Altava" title="Kingdom of Altava">
        Kingdom of Altava
       </a>
       " after its capital city and it fell during the
       <a href="/wiki/Early_Muslim_conquests" title="Early Muslim conquests">
        Islamic conquests
       </a>
       of the 700s.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Germanic_Italy">
        Germanic Italy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Western_Roman_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Germanic Italy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Odoacer_480ad.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="545" data-file-width="900" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Odoacer_480ad.jpg/220px-Odoacer_480ad.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Odoacer_480ad.jpg/330px-Odoacer_480ad.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Odoacer_480ad.jpg/440px-Odoacer_480ad.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Odoacer_480ad.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Odoacer" title="Odoacer">
          Odoacer
         </a>
         's Italy in 480 AD, following the annexation of
         <a href="/wiki/Dalmatia" title="Dalmatia">
          Dalmatia
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The deposition of
       <a href="/wiki/Romulus_Augustulus" title="Romulus Augustulus">
        Romulus Augustus
       </a>
       and rise of
       <a href="/wiki/Odoacer" title="Odoacer">
        Odoacer
       </a>
       as ruler of Italy in 476 received very little attention at the time.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_58-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-:4-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Overall, very little changed for the people; there was still a Roman Emperor in Constantinople that Odoacer had subordinated himself to. Throne vacances had been experienced at many points in the West before and the deposition of Romulus Augustus was nothing out of the ordinary. Odoacer saw his rule as entirely in the tradition of the Roman Empire, his role was not unlike that of
       <a href="/wiki/Ricimer" title="Ricimer">
        Ricimer
       </a>
       , and he effectively ruled as an imperial "governor" of Italy and was even awarded the title of
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Patrician_(ancient_Rome)" title="Patrician (ancient Rome)">
         patricius
        </a>
       </i>
       . Odoacer ruled using the Roman administrative systems already in place and continued to mint coins with the name and portrait of
       <a href="/wiki/Julius_Nepos" title="Julius Nepos">
        Julius Nepos
       </a>
       until 480 and later with the name and portrait of the Eastern
       <i>
        Augustus
       </i>
       , rather than in his own name.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_58-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-:4-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Solidus-Odoacer-ZenoRIC_3657cf.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="221" data-file-width="500" height="97" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Solidus-Odoacer-ZenoRIC_3657cf.jpg/220px-Solidus-Odoacer-ZenoRIC_3657cf.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Solidus-Odoacer-ZenoRIC_3657cf.jpg/330px-Solidus-Odoacer-ZenoRIC_3657cf.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Solidus-Odoacer-ZenoRIC_3657cf.jpg/440px-Solidus-Odoacer-ZenoRIC_3657cf.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Solidus-Odoacer-ZenoRIC_3657cf.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Solidus minted under
         <a href="/wiki/Odoacer" title="Odoacer">
          Odoacer
         </a>
         with the name and portrait of the Eastern Emperor
         <a href="/wiki/Zeno_(emperor)" title="Zeno (emperor)">
          Zeno
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       When Julius Nepos was murdered in Dalmatia in 480, Odoacer assumed the duty of pursuing and executing the assassins and established his own rule in Dalmatia at the same time.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
        <a href="#cite_note-64">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Odoacer established his power with the loyal support of the
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Senate" title="Roman Senate">
        Roman Senate
       </a>
       , a legislative body that had continued even without an emperor residing in Italy. Indeed, the Senate seems to have increased in power under Odoacer. For the first time since the mid-3rd century, copper coins were issued with the legend
       <i>
        S C
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        Senatus Consulto
       </i>
       ). These coins were copied by
       <a href="/wiki/Vandals" title="Vandals">
        Vandals
       </a>
       in Africa and also formed the basis of the currency reform done by Emperor
       <a href="/wiki/Anastasius_I_Dicorus" title="Anastasius I Dicorus">
        Anastasius
       </a>
       in the East.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
        <a href="#cite_note-65">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Under Odoacer, Western
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_consul" title="Roman consul">
        consuls
       </a>
       continued to be appointed as they had been under Western Roman Empire and were accepted by the Eastern Court, the first of these were
       <a href="/wiki/Caecina_Decius_Maximus_Basilius" title="Caecina Decius Maximus Basilius">
        Caecina Decius Maximus Basilus
       </a>
       in 480. Basilus was later also made the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Praetorian_prefect_of_Italy" title="Praetorian prefect of Italy">
        Preatorian Prefect of Italy
       </a>
       in 483, a position that continued to exist under Odoacer.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
        <a href="#cite_note-66">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
       11 further consuls were appointed by the Senate under Odoacer during his reign from 480 to 493 and one further Praetorian Prefect of Italy was appointed,
       <a href="/wiki/Caecina_Mavortius_Basilius_Decius" title="Caecina Mavortius Basilius Decius">
        Caecina Mavortius Basilius Decius
       </a>
       (486-493).
      </p>
      <p>
       Though Odoacer ruled as a Roman governor would have and maintained himself as a subordinate to the
       <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">
        remaining Empire
       </a>
       , the Eastern Emperor
       <a href="/wiki/Zeno_(emperor)" title="Zeno (emperor)">
        Zeno
       </a>
       began to increasingly see him as a rival. Thus, Zeno promised
       <a href="/wiki/Theoderic_the_Great" title="Theoderic the Great">
        Theoderic the Great
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Ostrogoths" title="Ostrogoths">
        Ostrogoths
       </a>
       ,
       <i>
        foederati
       </i>
       of the Eastern Court, control over the
       <a href="/wiki/Italian_Peninsula" title="Italian Peninsula">
        Italian peninsula
       </a>
       if they were able to defeat Odoacer.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
        <a href="#cite_note-67">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Theoderic leade the Ostrogoths across the
       <a href="/wiki/Julian_Alps" title="Julian Alps">
        Julian Alps
       </a>
       and into Italy in 489 and defeated Odoacer in battle twice the same year. Following four years of hostilities between them, John, the
       <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Ravenna" title="Bishop of Ravenna">
        Bishop of Ravenna
       </a>
       , was able to negotiate a treaty in 493 between Odoacer and Theoderic wherein they agreed to rule Ravenna and Italy jointly. Theoderic entered Ravenna on 5 March and Odoacer was dead ten days later, killed by Theoderic after sharing a meal with him.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
        <a href="#cite_note-68">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Empire_of_Theodoric_the_Great_523.gif">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="478" data-file-width="523" height="201" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Empire_of_Theodoric_the_Great_523.gif/220px-Empire_of_Theodoric_the_Great_523.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Empire_of_Theodoric_the_Great_523.gif/330px-Empire_of_Theodoric_the_Great_523.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Empire_of_Theodoric_the_Great_523.gif/440px-Empire_of_Theodoric_the_Great_523.gif 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Empire_of_Theodoric_the_Great_523.gif" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Map of the realm of
         <a href="/wiki/Theoderic_the_Great" title="Theoderic the Great">
          Theoderic the Great
         </a>
         at its height in 523, following the annexation of the southern parts of the
         <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Burgundians" title="Kingdom of the Burgundians">
          Burgundian kingdom
         </a>
         . Theoderic ruled both the
         <a href="/wiki/Visigothic_Kingdom" title="Visigothic Kingdom">
          Visigothic
         </a>
         and
         <a href="/wiki/Ostrogothic_Kingdom" title="Ostrogothic Kingdom">
          Ostrogothic kingdoms
         </a>
         and exerted hegemony over the Burgundians and
         <a href="/wiki/Vandal_Kingdom" title="Vandal Kingdom">
          Vandals
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Theoderic inherited the role of Odoacer, the acting viceroy for Italy and ostensibly a
       <i>
        patricius
       </i>
       and subject of the emperor in Constantinople. This position was recognized by Emperor
       <a href="/wiki/Anastasius_I_Dicorus" title="Anastasius I Dicorus">
        Anastasius
       </a>
       in 497. Though Theoderic acted as an independent ruler, he meticulously preserved the outward appearance of his subordinate position.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_69-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:5-69">
         [69]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Theoderic continued to use the administrative systems of Odoacer's kingdom, essentially those of the Western Roman Empire, and administrative positions continued to be staffed exclusively by Romans. The senate continued to function as it always had and the laws of the Empire were recognized as ruling the Roman population, though the Goths were ruled by their own traditional laws. As a subordinate, Theoderic did not have the right to issue his own
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_law" title="Roman law">
        laws
       </a>
       , only edicts or clarifications.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_69-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:5-69">
         [69]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The army and military offices were exclusively staffed by the Goths however, largely settled in northern Italy.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
        <a href="#cite_note-70">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Though acting as a subordinate in domestic affairs, Theoderic acted increasingly independent in his foreign policies. Seeking to counterbalance the influence of the Empire in the East, Theoderic married his daughters to the Visigothic king
       <a href="/wiki/Alaric_II" title="Alaric II">
        Alaric II
       </a>
       and the Burgundian prince
       <a href="/wiki/Sigismund_of_Burgundy" title="Sigismund of Burgundy">
        Sigismund
       </a>
       , his sister Amalfrida was married to the Vandal king
       <a href="/wiki/Thrasamund" title="Thrasamund">
        Thrasamund
       </a>
       and he married Audofleda, sister of the Frankish king
       <a href="/wiki/Clovis_I" title="Clovis I">
        Clovis I
       </a>
       , himself.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
        <a href="#cite_note-71">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Through these alliances and occasional conflicts, the territory controlled by Theoderic in the early sixth century nearly constituted a restored Western Roman Empire. Ruler of Italy since 493, Theoderic became
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_of_the_Visigoths" title="King of the Visigoths">
        king of the Visigoths
       </a>
       in 511 and exerted hegemony over the
       <a href="/wiki/Vandal_Kingdom" title="Vandal Kingdom">
        Vandals
       </a>
       in North Africa between 521 and 523. As such, his rule extended throughout the western
       <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">
        Mediterranean
       </a>
       . The western imperial regalia had been returned to
       <a href="/wiki/Ravenna" title="Ravenna">
        Ravenna
       </a>
       by the emperor
       <a href="/wiki/Anastasius_I_Dicorus" title="Anastasius I Dicorus">
        Anastasius
       </a>
       in 497 and Theoderic was essentially western emperor in all but name.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
        <a href="#cite_note-72">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       With the death of Theoderic in 526, his network of alliances began to collapse. The Visigoths regained autonomy under king
       <a href="/wiki/Amalaric" title="Amalaric">
        Amalaric
       </a>
       and the relations with the Vandals turned increasingly hostile under the reign of the new Ostrogothic king
       <a href="/wiki/Athalaric" title="Athalaric">
        Athalaric
       </a>
       , a child under the regency of his mother
       <a href="/wiki/Amalasuntha" title="Amalasuntha">
        Amalasuntha
       </a>
       . Amalasuntha intended to coninue the policies of conciliation between the Goths and Romans, supporting the new Eastern Emperor
       <a href="/wiki/Justinian_I" title="Justinian I">
        Justinian I
       </a>
       and allowing him to use Sicily as a staging point during the reconquest of Africa in the
       <a href="/wiki/Vandalic_War" title="Vandalic War">
        Vandalic War
       </a>
       . With the death of Athalaric in 534, Amalasuntha crowned her cousin and only relative
       <a href="/wiki/Theodahad" title="Theodahad">
        Theodahad
       </a>
       as king, hoping for his support. Instead, Amalasuntha was imprisoned and even though Theodahad assured Emperor Justinian of her safety, she was executed shortly thereafter. This served as an ideal cause of war for Justinian, who invaded Italy after Theodahad had refused to renounce his rule of the peninsula in favour of the Empire.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:7_73-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:7-73">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Barbarian_Kingdoms">
        Barbarian Kingdoms
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Western_Roman_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Barbarian Kingdoms">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Barbarian_kingdoms" title="Barbarian kingdoms">
        Barbarian kingdoms
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Europa_in_526.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="639" data-file-width="799" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Europa_in_526.png/220px-Europa_in_526.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Europa_in_526.png/330px-Europa_in_526.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Europa_in_526.png/440px-Europa_in_526.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Europa_in_526.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Map of the Barbarian Kingdoms of the western
         <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">
          Mediterranean
         </a>
         in 526, seven years before the campaigns of reconquest under
         <a href="/wiki/Justinian_I" title="Justinian I">
          Justinian I
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In the context of the Western Roman Empire, the term "barbarian kingdoms" most often refers to the Germanic kingdoms that sprung from the formerly Western Roman territory. Their beginnings, together with the end of the Western Roman Empire, marks the transition from
       <a href="/wiki/Late_antiquity" title="Late antiquity">
        Late Antiquity
       </a>
       to the
       <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">
        Middle Ages
       </a>
       . The barbarian kingdoms gradually replaced the old Roman system, specifically in the
       <a href="/wiki/Praetorian_prefecture" title="Praetorian prefecture">
        praetorian prefectures
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Praetorian_prefecture_of_Gaul" title="Praetorian prefecture of Gaul">
        Gaul
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Praetorian_prefecture_of_Italy" title="Praetorian prefecture of Italy">
        Italy
       </a>
       , during the sixth and seventh centuries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:10_74-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:10-74">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Visigoths_tremissis_6_century_823177.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="385" data-file-width="800" height="106" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Visigoths_tremissis_6_century_823177.jpg/220px-Visigoths_tremissis_6_century_823177.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Visigoths_tremissis_6_century_823177.jpg/330px-Visigoths_tremissis_6_century_823177.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Visigoths_tremissis_6_century_823177.jpg/440px-Visigoths_tremissis_6_century_823177.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Visigoths_tremissis_6_century_823177.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         6th-century Visigothic coin, struck in the name of Emperor
         <a href="/wiki/Justinian_I" title="Justinian I">
          Justinian I
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       There were several different kingdoms of differing size, power and origins. The
       <a href="/wiki/Visigothic_Kingdom" title="Visigothic Kingdom">
        Visigothic Kingdom
       </a>
       was the earliest one established, founded as a vassal state to the Western Roman Empire through the
       <a href="/wiki/Visigoths" title="Visigoths">
        Visigoths
       </a>
       being granted land in southern Gaul by Emperor
       <a href="/wiki/Honorius_(emperor)" title="Honorius (emperor)">
        Honorius
       </a>
       in 418.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:6_36-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:6-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       After its establishment, relations between the Visigoths and the Western court were mixed. Though federated vassals, the Visigoths remained
       <i>
        de facto
       </i>
       independent and began a rapid period of expansion at the expense of the Western empire. The Visigoths were thus periodically enemies with the Western court, though they had allied with the Western Roman army against the Huns and assisted in defeating Attila at the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Catalaunian_Plains" title="Battle of the Catalaunian Plains">
        Battle of the Catalaunian Plains
       </a>
       in 451. At the time of the collapse of the Western Empire in 476/480, the Visigoths controlled large swaths of Southern Gaul as well as a majority of
       <a href="/wiki/Hispania" title="Hispania">
        Hispania
       </a>
       , their increased domain having been partly conquered and partly awarded to them by the Western Emperor
       <a href="/wiki/Avitus" title="Avitus">
        Avitus
       </a>
       in the 450s-60s.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
        <a href="#cite_note-75">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Like the Germanic kingdoms of Italy, the Visigoths continued to recognise the Emperor in Constantinople as somewhat of a nominal sovereign, continuing to mint coins in their names until the reign of
       <a href="/wiki/Justinian_I" title="Justinian I">
        Justinian I
       </a>
       in the sixth century.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
        <a href="#cite_note-76">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Visigothic Kingdom continued to control most of the
       <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">
        Iberian peninsula
       </a>
       until it fell to the
       <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_Caliphate" title="Umayyad Caliphate">
        Umayyad Caliphate
       </a>
       in the 720s.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
        <a href="#cite_note-77">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Asturias" title="Kingdom of Asturias">
        Kingdom of Asturias
       </a>
       was founded by a Visigoth nobleman around the same time and remained the only bastion of
       <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">
        Christianity
       </a>
       on the peninsula until the
       <a href="/wiki/Reconquista" title="Reconquista">
        reconquista
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
        <a href="#cite_note-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Vandal_Kingdom" title="Vandal Kingdom">
        Vandal Kingdom
       </a>
       was founded through
       <a href="/wiki/Vandals" title="Vandals">
        Vandalic
       </a>
       conquests in the provinces of
       <a href="/wiki/Africa_(Roman_province)" title="Africa (Roman province)">
        Roman Africa
       </a>
       , culminating in a siege and subsequent conquest of Carthage in 439.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
        <a href="#cite_note-79">
         [79]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Vandals continually used an impressive fleet to loot the coasts of both the Western and Eastern halves of the Empire, becoming an increasingly strong naval power. After the death of Attila, the Romans made repeated efforts at recapturing Africa and destroying the Vandals, since they were in control of some of the richest imperial lands. With several planned campaigns never being carried out or being destroyed in naval battles, the Vandals remained a power and even sacked Rome in 455.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
        <a href="#cite_note-80">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Unlike the Visigoths, the Vandals minted their own coinage and were both
       <i>
        de facto
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        de jure
       </i>
       independent.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
        <a href="#cite_note-81">
         [81]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Just like the
       <a href="/wiki/Ostrogoths" title="Ostrogoths">
        Ostrogoths
       </a>
       of Italy, the Vandalic Kingdom would come to be reconquered under the western campaigns of Emperor Justinian I.
      </p>
      <p>
       After the collapse of
       <a href="/wiki/Theoderic_the_Great" title="Theoderic the Great">
        Theoderic the Great
       </a>
       's control of the western Mediterranean through alliances, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frankish_kingdom" title="Frankish kingdom">
        Frankish Kingdom
       </a>
       would rise to become the most powerful of the Barbarian Kingdoms, having taken control of most of Gaul in the absence of Roman governance. Under
       <a href="/wiki/Clovis_I" title="Clovis I">
        Clovis I
       </a>
       from the 480s to 511, the Franks would come to develop into a great regional power, conquering the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Domain_of_Soissons" title="Domain of Soissons">
        Domain of Soissons
       </a>
       in 481, defeating the
       <a href="/wiki/Alemanni" title="Alemanni">
        Alemanni
       </a>
       in 504 and conquering all Visigothic territory north of the north of the
       <a href="/wiki/Pyrenees" title="Pyrenees">
        Pyrenees
       </a>
       other than
       <a href="/wiki/Septimania" title="Septimania">
        Septimania
       </a>
       in 507. Unlike with the hostile Vandals, relations between the Franks and the Eastern Empire appear to have been rather positive, with Emperor
       <a href="/wiki/Anastasius_I_Dicorus" title="Anastasius I Dicorus">
        Anastasius
       </a>
       granting Clovis the title of
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_consul" title="Roman consul">
        consul
       </a>
       following his victory against the Visigoths.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
        <a href="#cite_note-82">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Frankish Kingdom would turn out to be the most stable of all the Barbarian kingdoms, eventually developing into the
       <a href="/wiki/Carolingian_Empire" title="Carolingian Empire">
        Carolingian Empire
       </a>
       and later
       <a href="/wiki/France_in_the_Middle_Ages" title="France in the Middle Ages">
        France
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">
        Holy Roman Empire
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Imperial_reconquest">
        Imperial reconquest
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Western_Roman_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Imperial reconquest">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Vandalic_War" title="Vandalic War">
        Vandalic War
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Gothic_War_(535%E2%80%93554)" title="Gothic War (535–554)">
        Gothic War (535–554)
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Justinien_527-565.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="871" data-file-width="1810" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Justinien_527-565.svg/250px-Justinien_527-565.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Justinien_527-565.svg/375px-Justinien_527-565.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Justinien_527-565.svg/500px-Justinien_527-565.svg.png 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Justinien_527-565.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Roman_Empire" title="Eastern Roman Empire">
          Eastern Roman Empire
         </a>
         , by reoccupying some of the former Western Roman Empire's lands, enlarged its territory considerably during
         <a href="/wiki/Justinian_I" title="Justinian I">
          Justinian
         </a>
         's reign from 527
         <i>
          (red)
         </i>
         to 565
         <i>
          (orange)
         </i>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       With Emperor Zeno having juridically reunified the Empire into one imperial court, the remaining Eastern Roman Empire continued to lay claim to the areas previously controlled by the Western court throughout
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Late_Antiquity" title="Late Antiquity">
        Late Antiquity
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">
        Middle Ages
       </a>
       . Though military campaigns had been conducted by the Western court prior to 476 with the aim of recapturing lost territory, most notably under
       <a href="/wiki/Majorian" title="Majorian">
        Majorian
       </a>
       , the reconquests, if successful at all, were only momentary. It was first under the campaigns of the generals
       <a href="/wiki/Belisarius" title="Belisarius">
        Belisarius
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Narses" title="Narses">
        Narses
       </a>
       on behalf of the Eastern Roman Emperor
       <a href="/wiki/Justinian_I" title="Justinian I">
        Justinian I
       </a>
       from 533 to 554 that long-lasting reconquests of Roman lands were witnessed.
      </p>
      <p>
       During the 6th century, the Eastern Roman Empire under Justinian managed to reconquer large areas of the former Western Roman Empire. With the pro-Roman Vandal king
       <a href="/wiki/Hilderic" title="Hilderic">
        Hilderic
       </a>
       having been deposed by
       <a href="/wiki/Gelimer" title="Gelimer">
        Gelimer
       </a>
       in 530
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
        <a href="#cite_note-83">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , Justinian prepared an expedition lead by prominent general Belisarius that swiftly retook North Africa from June 533 to March 534, returning the wealthy province to Roman rule. Following the reconquest, Justinian swiftly reestablished the Roman administrations of the province, establishing a new
       <a href="/wiki/Praetorian_prefecture_of_Africa" title="Praetorian prefecture of Africa">
        Praetorian Prefecture of Africa
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
        <a href="#cite_note-84">
         [84]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and taking measures to decrease vandal influence, eventually leading to the complete disappearance of the
       <a href="/wiki/Vandals" title="Vandals">
        vandalic people
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
        <a href="#cite_note-85">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:390px;max-width:390px">
        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
         <div class="thumbimage">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mosaic_of_Justinianus_I_-_Basilica_San_Vitale_(Ravenna).jpg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="2079" data-file-width="1500" height="277" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Mosaic_of_Justinianus_I_-_Basilica_San_Vitale_%28Ravenna%29.jpg/200px-Mosaic_of_Justinianus_I_-_Basilica_San_Vitale_%28Ravenna%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Mosaic_of_Justinianus_I_-_Basilica_San_Vitale_%28Ravenna%29.jpg/300px-Mosaic_of_Justinianus_I_-_Basilica_San_Vitale_%28Ravenna%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Mosaic_of_Justinianus_I_-_Basilica_San_Vitale_%28Ravenna%29.jpg/400px-Mosaic_of_Justinianus_I_-_Basilica_San_Vitale_%28Ravenna%29.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
          </a>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:184px;max-width:184px">
         <div class="thumbimage">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Manuel_I_Comnenus.jpg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="606" data-file-width="397" height="278" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Manuel_I_Comnenus.jpg/182px-Manuel_I_Comnenus.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Manuel_I_Comnenus.jpg/273px-Manuel_I_Comnenus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Manuel_I_Comnenus.jpg/364px-Manuel_I_Comnenus.jpg 2x" width="182"/>
          </a>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div style="clear:left">
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">
         <a href="/wiki/Justinian_I" title="Justinian I">
          Justinian I
         </a>
         (right) was the first Eastern Emperor to attempt to reconquer the territories of the Western Roman Empire, undertaking successful campaigns in Africa and Italy in the 500s.
         <a href="/wiki/Manuel_I_Komnenos" title="Manuel I Komnenos">
          Manuel I Komnenos
         </a>
         (right) was the last, campaigning in southern Italy in the 1150s.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Following the execution of the pro-Roman Ostrogoth queen
       <a href="/wiki/Amalasuntha" title="Amalasuntha">
        Amalasuntha
       </a>
       and the refusal of Ostrogoth king
       <a href="/wiki/Theodahad" title="Theodahad">
        Theodahad
       </a>
       to renounce his control of Italy, Justinian ordered the expedition to move on to reconquer Italy
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:7_73-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:7-73">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , ancient heartland of the Empire. From 534 to 540, the Roman forces campaigned in Italy and captured Ravenna, the Ostrogothic and formerly Western Roman capital, in 540. The Gothic resistance revived under king Totila in 541, and they were only defeated following campaigns by the Roman general
       <a href="/wiki/Narses" title="Narses">
        Narses
       </a>
       , who also repelled invasions into Italy by the
       <a href="/wiki/Franks" title="Franks">
        Franks
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Alemanni" title="Alemanni">
        Alemanni
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
        <a href="#cite_note-86">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Justinian promulgated the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pragmatic_Sanction" title="Pragmatic Sanction">
        Pragmatic Sanction
       </a>
       to reorganize the governance of Italy and the province was returned to Roman rule, though some cities in northern Italy continued to hold out until the 560s. The end of the conflict saw Italy devastated and considerably depopulated, which made it difficult to retain over the following centuries.
      </p>
      <p>
       Justinian also undertook limited campaigns against the
       <a href="/wiki/Visigothic_Kingdom" title="Visigothic Kingdom">
        Visigoths
       </a>
       , recovering portions of the southern coast of the
       <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">
        Iberian peninsula
       </a>
       . Here, the province of
       <a href="/wiki/Spania" title="Spania">
        Spania
       </a>
       would last until the 620s, when the Visigoths under king
       <a href="/wiki/Suintila" title="Suintila">
        Suintila
       </a>
       reconquered the southern coast.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
        <a href="#cite_note-87">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       These regions remained under Roman control throughout the reign of Justinian. Only three years after his death, the
       <a href="/wiki/Lombards" title="Lombards">
        Lombards
       </a>
       invaded Italy. Through conquests of the devastated peninsula, the Lombards conquered large parts of Italy in the late 500s, establishing the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lombard_Kingdom" title="Lombard Kingdom">
        Lombard Kingdom
       </a>
       . The Lombards were in constant conflict with the
       <a href="/wiki/Exarchate_of_Ravenna" title="Exarchate of Ravenna">
        Exarchate of Ravenna
       </a>
       , a polity established to replace the old
       <a href="/wiki/Praetorian_prefecture_of_Italy" title="Praetorian prefecture of Italy">
        Praetorian Prefecture of Italy
       </a>
       and enforcing Roman rule in Italy. The wealthiest parts of the province, including the cities of
       <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">
        Rome
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Ravenna" title="Ravenna">
        Ravenna
       </a>
       , remained securely in Roman hands under the Exarchate throughout the seventh century.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
        <a href="#cite_note-88">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ByzantineEmpire717AD2lightpurple.PNG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="370" data-file-width="800" height="102" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/ByzantineEmpire717AD2lightpurple.PNG/220px-ByzantineEmpire717AD2lightpurple.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/ByzantineEmpire717AD2lightpurple.PNG/330px-ByzantineEmpire717AD2lightpurple.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/ByzantineEmpire717AD2lightpurple.PNG/440px-ByzantineEmpire717AD2lightpurple.PNG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ByzantineEmpire717AD2lightpurple.PNG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Map of the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Roman_empire" title="Eastern Roman empire">
          Eastern Roman Empire
         </a>
         in 717 AD, over the course of the seventh and eighth centuries, Islamic expansion had ended Roman rule in Africa and though some bastions of Roman rule remained, most of Italy was controlled by the
         <a href="/wiki/Lombards" title="Lombards">
          Lombards
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Although some eastern emperors occasionally attempted to campaign in the West, none were as successful as Justinian. After 600, events conspired to drive the Western provinces out of Constantinople's control, with imperial attention focused on the pressing issues of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Byzantine-Sassanid_War_of_602-628" title="Byzantine-Sassanid War of 602-628">
        war with Sasanian Persia
       </a>
       and then the rise of Islam. For a while, the West remained important, with the
       <a href="/wiki/Constans_II" title="Constans II">
        Emperor Constans II
       </a>
       ruling from
       <a href="/wiki/Syracuse,_Sicily" title="Syracuse, Sicily">
        Syracuse
       </a>
       in Sicily a Roman Empire that still stretched from North Africa to the Caucasus in the 660s, but thereafter imperial attention declined rapidly, with Constantinople itself being besieged in the 670s, renewed war with the Arabs in the 680s, and then a period of chaos between 695 and 717, during which time Africa was finally lost to the Romans once and for all, being conquered by the
       <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_Caliphate" title="Umayyad Caliphate">
        Umayyad Caliphate
       </a>
       . Through reforms and military campaigns, Emperor Leo III attempted to restore order in the Empire, but his doctrinal reforms, known as the
       <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Iconoclasm" title="Byzantine Iconoclasm">
        Iconoclastic Controversy
       </a>
       , were extremely unpopular in the West and were condemned by
       <a href="/wiki/Pope_Gregory_III" title="Pope Gregory III">
        Pope Gregory III
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
        <a href="#cite_note-89">
         [89]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This led to the final breakdown in imperial rule over Rome itself, and the gradual transition of the Exarchate of Ravenna into the independent
       <a href="/wiki/Papal_States" title="Papal States">
        Papal States
       </a>
       , lead by the Pope. In an attempt at gaining support against the Lombards, the Pope called for aid from the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frankish_kingdom" title="Frankish kingdom">
        Frankish Kingdom
       </a>
       instead of the Eastern Empire, eventually crowning the Frankish king
       <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">
        Charlemagne
       </a>
       as "Roman Emperor" in 800 AD. Though this coronation was strongly opposed by the Eastern Empire, there was little they could do as their influence in Western Europe decreased.
      </p>
      <p>
       Imperial rule continued in
       <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">
        Sicily
       </a>
       throughout the eighth century, with the island slowly being overrun by the Arabs over the course of the ninth century. In Italy, a few strongholds in
       <a href="/wiki/Calabria" title="Calabria">
        Calabria
       </a>
       ultimately provided a base for modest imperial expansion, which reached its peak in the early eleventh century, with most of southern Italy under Roman rule of a sort. This, however, was undone by further civil wars in the empire, and the slow conquest of the region by the Empires' former mercenaries, the
       <a href="/wiki/Normans" title="Normans">
        Normans
       </a>
       , who finally put an end to imperial rule in Western Europe in 1071 with the
       <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Bari" title="Siege of Bari">
        conquest of Bari
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
        <a href="#cite_note-90">
         [90]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The last Emperor to attempt reconquests in the West was
       <a href="/wiki/Manuel_I_Komnenos" title="Manuel I Komnenos">
        Manuel I Komnenos
       </a>
       , who invaded Southern Italy during a war with the Norman
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Sicily" title="Kingdom of Sicily">
        Kingdom of Sicily
       </a>
       in the 1150s. The city of
       <a href="/wiki/Bari" title="Bari">
        Bari
       </a>
       willingly opened its gates to the Emperor
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
        <a href="#cite_note-91">
         [91]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and facing successes in the taking of other cities in the region, Manuel dreamed of a restored Roman Empire and a union between the churches of
       <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">
        Rome
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">
        Constantinople
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
        <a href="#cite_note-92">
         [92]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , separated since the
       <a href="/wiki/East%E2%80%93West_Schism" title="East–West Schism">
        schism of 1054
       </a>
       . Despite initial successes and Papal support, the campaign was unsuccessful and Manuel was forced to return East.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
        <a href="#cite_note-93">
         [93]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Nomenclature">
        Nomenclature
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Western_Roman_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Nomenclature">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Marcellinus_Comes" title="Marcellinus Comes">
        Marcellinus Comes
       </a>
       , a sixth century Eastern Roman historian and a courtier of
       <a href="/wiki/Justinian_I" title="Justinian I">
        Justinian I
       </a>
       , mentions the Western Roman Empire at some points in his
       <i>
        Chronicle
       </i>
       , which primarily covers the Eastern Roman Empire from 379 to 534. In the
       <i>
        Chronicle
       </i>
       , it is made clear that Marcellinus made a clear divide between East and West, with both mentions of a geographical east ("
       <i>
        Oriens
       </i>
       ") and west ("
       <i>
        Occidens
       </i>
       ") and an imperial east ("
       <i>
        Orientale imperium
       </i>
       " and "
       <i>
        Orientale respublica
       </i>
       ") and an imperial west ("
       <i>
        Occidentalie imperium
       </i>
       ", "
       <i>
        Occidentale regnum
       </i>
       ", "
       <i>
        Occidentalis respublica
       </i>
       ", "
       <i>
        Hesperium regnum
       </i>
       ", "
       <i>
        Hesperium imperium
       </i>
       " and "
       <i>
        principatum Occidentis
       </i>
       "). Furthermore, Marcellinus specifically designates some emperors and consuls as being "Eastern", "
       <i>
        Orientalibus principibus
       </i>
       " and "
       <i>
        Orientalium consulum
       </i>
       " respectively.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:02_94-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:02-94">
         [94]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The term
       <i>
        Hesperium Imperium
       </i>
       , simply translating to "Western Empire", has sometimes been applied to the Western Roman Empire by modern historians as well.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
        <a href="#cite_note-95">
         [95]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
        <a href="#cite_note-96">
         [96]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Though Marcellinus does not refer to the Empire as a whole after 395, only referring specifically to its separate halves, he clearly identifies the term "Roman" as applying to the Empire as a whole. When using terms such as "us", "our generals" and "our emperor", Marcellinus distinguished both divisions of the Empire from outside foes such as the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sassanid_Persians" title="Sassanid Persians">
        Sassanid Persians
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Huns" title="Huns">
        Huns
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:02_94-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:02-94">
         [94]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This view is consistent with the knowledge that contemporary Romans of the fourth and fifth century continued to consider the Empire as a single unit, though sometimes with two rulers (as there had been many times in the past).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
        <a href="#cite_note-97">
         [97]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economical_decline">
        Economical decline
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Western_Roman_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Economical decline">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:0418_Befreiung_einer_belagerten_Stadt_Bodemuseum_anagoria.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4752" data-file-width="2189" height="478" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/0418_Befreiung_einer_belagerten_Stadt_Bodemuseum_anagoria.JPG/220px-0418_Befreiung_einer_belagerten_Stadt_Bodemuseum_anagoria.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/0418_Befreiung_einer_belagerten_Stadt_Bodemuseum_anagoria.JPG/330px-0418_Befreiung_einer_belagerten_Stadt_Bodemuseum_anagoria.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/0418_Befreiung_einer_belagerten_Stadt_Bodemuseum_anagoria.JPG/440px-0418_Befreiung_einer_belagerten_Stadt_Bodemuseum_anagoria.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:0418_Befreiung_einer_belagerten_Stadt_Bodemuseum_anagoria.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Stone-carved
         <a href="/wiki/Relief" title="Relief">
          relief
         </a>
         depicting the liberation of a besieged city by a relief force, with those defending the walls making a
         <a href="/wiki/Sortie" title="Sortie">
          sortie
         </a>
         (i.e. a sudden attack against a besieging enemy from within the besieged town); Western Roman Empire, early 5th century AD
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Rome and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_peninsula" title="Italian peninsula">
        Italian peninsula
       </a>
       began to experience an economic slowdown as industries and money began to move outward. By the beginning of the 2nd century AD, the economic stagnation of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italia_(Roman_province)" title="Italia (Roman province)">
        Italia
       </a>
       was seen in the
       <a href="/wiki/Province" title="Province">
        provincial-born
       </a>
       Emperors, such as
       <a href="/wiki/Trajan" title="Trajan">
        Trajan
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Hadrian" title="Hadrian">
        Hadrian
       </a>
       . Economic problems increased in strength and frequency.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The West, less urbanized with a spread-out populace, may have experienced an economic decline throughout the Late Empire in some provinces. Southern Italy, northern Gaul (except for large towns and cities) to some extent Spain and the Danubian areas may have suffered. The East was not so destitute, especially as Emperors like
       <a href="/wiki/Constantine_the_Great" title="Constantine the Great">
        Constantine the Great
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Constantius_II" title="Constantius II">
        Constantius II
       </a>
       had invested heavily in the eastern economy. As a result, the Eastern Empire could afford large numbers of professional soldiers and augment them with mercenaries, while the Western Roman Empire could not afford this to the same extent. Even in major defeats, the East could, certainly not without difficulties, buy off its enemies with a ransom.
      </p>
      <p>
       The political, economic and military control of the Eastern Empire's resources remained safe in Constantinople, which was well fortified and located at the crossroads of several major trade and military routes. In contrast, the Western Empire was more fragmented. Its capital was transferred to
       <a href="/wiki/Ravenna" title="Ravenna">
        Ravenna
       </a>
       in 402 largely for defensive reasons, and it had easy access to the imperial fleet of the Eastern Empire but was isolated in other aspects as it was surrounded by swamps and marshes. The economic power remained focused on Rome and its hyper-rich senatorial aristocracy which dominated much of Italy and Africa in particular. After
       <a href="/wiki/Gallienus" title="Gallienus">
        Gallienus
       </a>
       banned senators from army commands in the mid-3rd century, the senatorial elite lost all experience of—and interest in—military life. In the early 5th century the wealthy landowning elite of the Roman Senate largely barred its tenants from military service, but it also refused to approve sufficient funding for maintaining a sufficiently powerful mercenary army to defend the entire Western Empire. The West's most important military area had been northern Gaul and the Rhine frontier in the 4th century, when
       <a href="/wiki/Trier" title="Trier">
        Trier
       </a>
       frequently served as the capital of the Empire and many leading Western generals were
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Barbarians" title="Barbarians">
        Barbarians
       </a>
       . After the civil war in 394 between
       <a href="/wiki/Theodosius_I" title="Theodosius I">
        Theodosius I
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Eugenius" title="Eugenius">
        Eugenius
       </a>
       , the new Western government installed by Theodosius I increasingly had to divert military resources from Britain and the Rhine to protect Italy. This, in turn, led to further rebellions and civil wars because the Western imperial government was not providing the military protection the northern provinces expected and needed against the barbarians.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Western Empire's resources were much limited, and the lack of available manpower forced the government to rely ever more on confederate barbarian troops operating under their own commanders, where the Western Empire would often have difficulties paying. In certain cases deals were struck with the leaders of barbaric mercenaries rewarding them with land, which led to the Empire's decline as less land meant there would be less tax revenue to support the military.
      </p>
      <p>
       As the central power weakened, the State gradually lost control of its borders and provinces, as well as control over the
       <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">
        Mediterranean Sea
       </a>
       . Roman Emperors tried to maintain control of the sea, but, once the
       <a href="/wiki/Vandals" title="Vandals">
        Vandals
       </a>
       conquered
       <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">
        North Africa
       </a>
       , imperial authorities had to cover too much ground with too few resources. The loss of the African provinces might have been the worse reversal on the West's fortunes, since they were among its wealthiest territories and supplied the essential grain imports to Italy.
