In many places, the Roman institutions collapsed along with the economic stability. In some regions, such as Gaul and Italy, the settlement of barbarians on former Roman lands seems to have caused relatively little disruption.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">
        Legacy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Western_Roman_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Legacy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Legacy_of_the_Roman_Empire" title="Legacy of the Roman Empire">
        Legacy of the Roman Empire
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">
        Romance languages
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Corpus_Juris_Civilis" title="Corpus Juris Civilis">
        Corpus Juris Civilis
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Civil_law_(legal_system)" title="Civil law (legal system)">
        Civil law (legal system)
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Latin_alphabet" title="Latin alphabet">
        Latin alphabet
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Literature" title="Literature">
        Literature
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Bust_(sculpture)" title="Bust (sculpture)">
        Bust (sculpture)
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Concrete" title="Concrete">
        Concrete
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cities" title="Cities">
        Cities
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:308px;max-width:308px">
        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:132px;max-width:132px">
         <div class="thumbimage">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Consular_diptych_Probus_406.jpg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="1820" data-file-width="904" height="262" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Consular_diptych_Probus_406.jpg/130px-Consular_diptych_Probus_406.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Consular_diptych_Probus_406.jpg/195px-Consular_diptych_Probus_406.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Consular_diptych_Probus_406.jpg/260px-Consular_diptych_Probus_406.jpg 2x" width="130"/>
          </a>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:172px;max-width:172px">
         <div class="thumbimage">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Consular_diptych_Constantius_III.jpg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="1844" data-file-width="1200" height="261" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Consular_diptych_Constantius_III.jpg/170px-Consular_diptych_Constantius_III.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Consular_diptych_Constantius_III.jpg/255px-Consular_diptych_Constantius_III.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Consular_diptych_Constantius_III.jpg/340px-Consular_diptych_Constantius_III.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
          </a>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div style="clear:left">
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">
         <b>
          On the left
         </b>
         :
         <a href="/wiki/Honorius_(emperor)" title="Honorius (emperor)">
          Emperor Honorius
         </a>
         on the
         <a href="/wiki/Consular_diptych" title="Consular diptych">
          consular diptych
         </a>
         of
         <a href="/wiki/Anicius_Petronius_Probus" title="Anicius Petronius Probus">
          Anicius Petronius Probus
         </a>
         (406)
         <br/>
         <b>
          On the right
         </b>
         :
         <a href="/wiki/Consular_diptych" title="Consular diptych">
          Consular diptych
         </a>
         of
         <a href="/wiki/Constantius_III" title="Constantius III">
          Constantius III
         </a>
         (a co-emperor with Honorius in 421), produced for
         <a href="/wiki/Roman_consul" title="Roman consul">
          his consulate
         </a>
         in 413 or 417
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       As the Western Roman Empire crumbled, the new Germanic rulers who conquered the provinces upheld many Roman laws and traditions. Many of the invading Germanic tribes were already Christianized, although most were followers of
       <a href="/wiki/Arianism" title="Arianism">
        Arianism
       </a>
       . They quickly converted to
       <a href="/wiki/State_church_of_the_Roman_Empire" title="State church of the Roman Empire">
        official imperial Christianity
       </a>
       , gaining more loyalty from the local Roman populations, as well as the recognition and support of the powerful
       <a href="/wiki/Bishop" title="Bishop">
        Bishop
       </a>
       of Rome. Although they initially continued to recognize indigenous tribal laws, they were more influenced by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Law" title="Roman Law">
        Roman Law
       </a>
       and gradually incorporated it as well.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:10_74-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:10-74">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Roman Law, particularly the
       <a href="/wiki/Corpus_Juris_Civilis" title="Corpus Juris Civilis">
        Corpus Juris Civilis
       </a>
       collected by order of Justinian I, is the ancient basis on which the modern
       <a href="/wiki/Civil_law_(legal_system)" title="Civil law (legal system)">
        Civil law
       </a>
       stands. In contrast,
       <a href="/wiki/Common_law" title="Common law">
        Common law
       </a>
       is based on the Germanic
       <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxon_law" title="Anglo-Saxon law">
        Anglo-Saxon law
       </a>
       . Civil law is by far the most widespread system of law in the world, in force in some form in about 150 countries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
        <a href="#cite_note-98">
         [98]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Romance_languages.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1525" data-file-width="2100" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Romance_languages.png/220px-Romance_languages.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Romance_languages.png/330px-Romance_languages.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Romance_languages.png/440px-Romance_languages.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Romance_languages.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Romance_language" title="Romance language">
          Romance languages
         </a>
         , languages that developed from
         <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">
          Latin
         </a>
         following the collapse of the Western Roman Empire, are spoken in
         <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">
          Western Europe
         </a>
         to this day and their spread almost reflect the continental borders of the old Empire.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_(language)" title="Latin (language)">
        Latin
       </a>
       as a language never really disappeared.
       <a href="/wiki/Vulgar_Latin" title="Vulgar Latin">
        Vulgar Latin
       </a>
       combined with neighboring Germanic and
       <a href="/wiki/Celtic_languages" title="Celtic languages">
        Celtic languages
       </a>
       , giving rise to many modern
       <a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">
        Romance languages
       </a>
       such as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_(language)" title="Italian (language)">
        Italian
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_(language)" title="French (language)">
        French
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_(language)" title="Spanish (language)">
        Spanish
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portuguese_(language)" title="Portuguese (language)">
        Portuguese
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Romanian_(language)" title="Romanian (language)">
        Romanian
       </a>
       and a large number of minor languages and dialects. Today, more than 900 million people are native speakers worldwide. In addition, many Romance languages are used throughout the world as
       <a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">
        lingua francas
       </a>
       by non-native speakers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
        <a href="#cite_note-99">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Latin also influenced
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Germanic_(language)" title="Germanic (language)">
        Germanic languages
       </a>
       such as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/English_(language)" title="English (language)">
        English
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
        <a href="#cite_note-100">
         [100]
        </a>
       </sup>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_(language)" title="German (language)">
        German
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
        <a href="#cite_note-101">
         [101]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dutch_(language)" title="Dutch (language)">
        Dutch
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
        <a href="#cite_note-102">
         [102]
        </a>
       </sup>
       ; all surviving
       <a href="/wiki/Celtic_languages" title="Celtic languages">
        Celtic languages
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
        <a href="#cite_note-103">
         [103]
        </a>
       </sup>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Albanian_(language)" title="Albanian (language)">
        Albanian
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
        <a href="#cite_note-104">
         [104]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , and such
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slavic_Languages" title="Slavic Languages">
        Slavic languages
       </a>
       as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polish_(language)" title="Polish (language)">
        Polish
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
        <a href="#cite_note-105">
         [105]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Czech_(language)" title="Czech (language)">
        Czech
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
        <a href="#cite_note-106">
         [106]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , and even the non-Indo-European
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hungarian_(language)" title="Hungarian (language)">
        Hungarian
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
        <a href="#cite_note-107">
         [107]
        </a>
       </sup>
       . It survives in its "purer" form
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">
        <a href="#cite_note-108">
         [note 1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       as the language of the Catholic Church
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">
        <a href="#cite_note-109">
         [108]
        </a>
       </sup>
       (the
       <a href="/wiki/Mass_(liturgy)" title="Mass (liturgy)">
        Mass
       </a>
       was spoken exclusively in Latin until
       <a href="/wiki/Ecclesiastical_Latin" title="Ecclesiastical Latin">
        1969
       </a>
       ), and was used as a
       <a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">
        lingua franca
       </a>
       between many nations. It remained the language of medicine, law, diplomacy (most treaties were written in Latin), of intellectuals and scholarship.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Latin_alphabet" title="Latin alphabet">
        Latin alphabet
       </a>
       was expanded due to the splits of I into I and J and of U into U, V, and in places (especially Germanic languages and Polish) W; it is the most widely used alphabetic writing system in the world today.
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_numerals" title="Roman numerals">
        Roman numerals
       </a>
       continue to be used, but were mostly replaced by
       <a href="/wiki/Arabic_numerals" title="Arabic numerals">
        Arabic numerals
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">
        <a href="#cite_note-110">
         [109]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       A very visible legacy of the Western Roman Empire is the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" title="Roman Catholic Church">
        Roman Catholic Church
       </a>
       . The Church slowly began to replace Roman institutions in the West, even helping to negotiate the safety of Rome during the late 5th century.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_40-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-:2-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In many cases the only source of law and civil administration was the local bishop, often himself a former governor like
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Ambrose" title="St. Ambrose">
        St. Ambrose
       </a>
       of Milan and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Germanus" title="St. Germanus">
        St. Germanus
       </a>
       of Auxerre. As Rome was invaded by Germanic tribes, many assimilated, and by the middle of the medieval period (c. 9th and 10th centuries) the central, western, and northern parts of
       <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">
        Europe
       </a>
       had been largely converted to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" title="Roman Catholic Church">
        Roman Catholicism
       </a>
       and acknowledged the Pope as the
       <a href="/wiki/Vicar_of_Christ" title="Vicar of Christ">
        Vicar of Christ
       </a>
       . The first of the Barbarian kings to convert to the church of Rome was
       <a href="/wiki/Clovis_I" title="Clovis I">
        Clovis I
       </a>
       of the Franks and other kingdoms, such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Visigothic_Kingdom" title="Visigothic Kingdom">
        Visigoths
       </a>
       , later followed suit to garner favor with the papacy.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111">
        <a href="#cite_note-111">
         [110]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Following the reconquest of Italy under Emperor
       <a href="/wiki/Justinian_I" title="Justinian I">
        Justinian I
       </a>
       , the popes were largely subservient to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exarch_of_Ravenna" title="Exarch of Ravenna">
        Exarchs of Ravenna
       </a>
       (the imperial representative in Italy). This humiliation, alongside the increasing amounts of territory lost by the Empire to the
       <a href="/wiki/Early_Muslim_conquests" title="Early Muslim conquests">
        Islamic conquests
       </a>
       and the inability to protect Italy against the
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Lombards" title="Kingdom of the Lombards">
        Lombards
       </a>
       , prompted
       <a href="/wiki/Pope_Stephen_II" title="Pope Stephen II">
        Pope Stephen II
       </a>
       to turn from the Eastern Emperor
       <a href="/wiki/Constantine_V" title="Constantine V">
        Constantine V
       </a>
       . Instead he appealed to the Frankish king
       <a href="/wiki/Pepin_the_Short" title="Pepin the Short">
        Pepin
       </a>
       , who subdued the Lombards and donated lands to the papacy. When
       <a href="/wiki/Pope_Leo_III" title="Pope Leo III">
        Pope Leo III
       </a>
       crowned
       <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">
        Charlemagne
       </a>
       as "Roman Emperor" in 800, he both severed ties with the outraged Eastern Empire and established the precedent that no man in Western Europe would be emperor without a papal coronation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">
        <a href="#cite_note-112">
         [111]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Though the power the Pope wielded changed significantly throughout the subsequent
       <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">
        Middle Ages
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Modern_period" title="Modern period">
        Modern period
       </a>
       , the office remains as the head of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_church" title="Roman Catholic church">
        Roman Catholic Church
       </a>
       and the head of state of the
       <a href="/wiki/Vatican_City" title="Vatican City">
        Vatican City
       </a>
       , the smallest sovereign state in the world. The Pope has consistently held the title of "
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pontifex_Maximus" title="Pontifex Maximus">
        Pontifex Maximus
       </a>
       " since before the fall of the Western Roman Empire and retains it to this day
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113">
        <a href="#cite_note-113">
         [112]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , a title formerly used by the high priest of the old
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Polytheism" title="Roman Polytheism">
        Roman polytheism
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Though gone in modern times, the
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Senate" title="Roman Senate">
        Roman Senate
       </a>
       survived the initial collapse of the Western Roman Empire. Its authority even seems to have increased under the rule of Italy by
       <a href="/wiki/Odoacer" title="Odoacer">
        Odoacer
       </a>
       and later the
       <a href="/wiki/Ostrogoths" title="Ostrogoths">
        Ostrogoths
       </a>
       , evident by that the senate in 498 managed to install
       <a href="/wiki/Pope_Symmachus" title="Pope Symmachus">
        Symmachus
       </a>
       as pope despite both
       <a href="/wiki/Theoderic_the_Great" title="Theoderic the Great">
        Theoderic
       </a>
       of Italy and emperor
       <a href="/wiki/Anastasius_I_Dicorus" title="Anastasius I Dicorus">
        Anastasius
       </a>
       supporting the other candidate,
       <a href="/wiki/Antipope_Laurentius" title="Antipope Laurentius">
        Laurentius
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114">
        <a href="#cite_note-114">
         [113]
        </a>
       </sup>
       When exactly the senate disappeared is unclear, it is known that the institution remained into the sixth century as gifts from the senate were received by emperor
       <a href="/wiki/Tiberius_II_Constantine" title="Tiberius II Constantine">
        Tiberius II
       </a>
       in 578 and 580 in hope of aid against the invading
       <a href="/wiki/Lombards" title="Lombards">
        Lombards
       </a>
       . The traditional senate building,
       <a href="/wiki/Curia_Julia" title="Curia Julia">
        Curia Julia
       </a>
       , was rebuilt into a church under pope
       <a href="/wiki/Pope_Honorius_I" title="Pope Honorius I">
        Honorius I
       </a>
       in 630, probably with permission from the eastern emperor
       <a href="/wiki/Heraclius" title="Heraclius">
        Heraclius
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115">
        <a href="#cite_note-115">
         [114]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Attempted_restorations">
        Attempted restorations
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Western_Roman_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Attempted restorations">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Exarchate_of_Ravenna_600_AD.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="396" data-file-width="694" height="126" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Exarchate_of_Ravenna_600_AD.png/220px-Exarchate_of_Ravenna_600_AD.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Exarchate_of_Ravenna_600_AD.png/330px-Exarchate_of_Ravenna_600_AD.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Exarchate_of_Ravenna_600_AD.png/440px-Exarchate_of_Ravenna_600_AD.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Exarchate_of_Ravenna_600_AD.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Exarchate_of_Ravenna" title="Exarchate of Ravenna">
          Exarchate of Ravenna
         </a>
         within the Roman Empire in 600 AD. The Exarchates of Ravenna and
         <a href="/wiki/Exarchate_of_Africa" title="Exarchate of Africa">
          Africa
         </a>
         were established by the Eastern Empire to better administrate the reconquered Western territories.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The positions of Eastern and Western
       <i>
        Augustus
       </i>
       , established under Emperor
       <a href="/wiki/Diocletian" title="Diocletian">
        Diocletian
       </a>
       in 286 as the
       <a href="/wiki/Tetrarchy" title="Tetrarchy">
        Tetrarchy
       </a>
       , had been abolished by Emperor
       <a href="/wiki/Zeno_(emperor)" title="Zeno (emperor)">
        Zeno
       </a>
       in 480 following the loss of direct control over the western territories. Declaring himself the sole
       <i>
        Augustus
       </i>
       , Zeno only exercised true control over the largely intact Eastern Empire and over Italy as the nominal overlord of
       <a href="/wiki/Odoacer" title="Odoacer">
        Odoacer
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:11_60-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:11-60">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
       With the reconquests under
       <a href="/wiki/Justinian_I" title="Justinian I">
        Justinian I
       </a>
       and the significant expansion of territory they brought, the Empire began to face the same problems it had faced during previous periods where there was only one ruler. As such, the idea of splitting the imperial court into two once more to more effectively govern the territory of the Empire resurfaced in the East.
      </p>
      <p>
       The earliest attempt at crowning a new Western Emperor after the abolition of the title
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">
        <a href="#cite_note-116">
         [115]
        </a>
       </sup>
       occurred already during the
       <a href="/wiki/Gothic_War_(535%E2%80%93554)" title="Gothic War (535–554)">
        Gothic Wars
       </a>
       under Justinian.
       <a href="/wiki/Belisarius" title="Belisarius">
        Belisarius
       </a>
       , an accomplished general that had already successfully campaigned to restore Roman control over North Africa and large parts of Italy (including Rome itself), was offered the position of Western Roman Emperor by the
       <a href="/wiki/Ostrogothic_Kingdom" title="Ostrogothic Kingdom">
        Ostrogoths
       </a>
       during his siege of
       <a href="/wiki/Ravenna" title="Ravenna">
        Ravenna
       </a>
       (the Ostrogothic, and previously Western Roman, capital) in 540. The Ostrogoths, desperate to avoid losing their control of Italy, offered the title and fealty to Belisarius as Western
       <i>
        Augustus
       </i>
       . Loyal to Justinian (who hoped to rule over a restored Roman Empire alone),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">
        <a href="#cite_note-117">
         [116]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Belisarius feigned to accept the title to enter the city, whereupon he immediately relinquished it. Despite Belisarius relinquishing the title, the offer had made Justinian suspicious and Belisarius was ordered to return east.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">
        <a href="#cite_note-118">
         [117]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       At the end of emperor
       <a href="/wiki/Tiberius_II_Constantine" title="Tiberius II Constantine">
        Tiberius II
       </a>
       's reign in 582, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Roman_empire" title="Eastern Roman empire">
        Eastern Roman Empire
       </a>
       retained control over relatively large parts of the regions reconquered under Justinian. Tiberius chose two
       <i>
        Caesares
       </i>
       , the general
       <a href="/wiki/Maurice_(emperor)" title="Maurice (emperor)">
        Maurice
       </a>
       and the governor
       <a href="/wiki/Germanus_(Caesar)" title="Germanus (Caesar)">
        Germanus
       </a>
       , and married his two daughters to them. Germanus had clear connections to the western provinces, and Maurice to the eastern provinces. It is possible that Tiberius had planned to divide the empire into western and eastern administrative units once more
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">
        <a href="#cite_note-119">
         [118]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , but if those plans existed they were never realized. At the death of Tiberius, Maurice inherited the entire empire as Germanus had refused the throne.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">
        <a href="#cite_note-120">
         [119]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Maurice would come to establish a new type of administrative unit, the
       <a href="/wiki/Exarchate" title="Exarchate">
        Exarchates
       </a>
       , and organized the remaining western territories under his control into two such exarchates; the Exarchates of
       <a href="/wiki/Exarchate_of_Ravenna" title="Exarchate of Ravenna">
        Ravenna
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Exarchate_of_Africa" title="Exarchate of Africa">
        Africa
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Restoration_of_the_Imperial_title_in_the_West">
        Restoration of the Imperial title in the West
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Western_Roman_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Restoration of the Imperial title in the West">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Frankish_Empire_(orthographic_projection).svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="550" data-file-width="551" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Frankish_Empire_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg/220px-Frankish_Empire_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Frankish_Empire_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg/330px-Frankish_Empire_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Frankish_Empire_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg/440px-Frankish_Empire_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Frankish_Empire_(orthographic_projection).svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Map of the
         <a href="/wiki/Carolingian_Empire" title="Carolingian Empire">
          Carolingian Empire
         </a>
         under
         <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">
          Charlemagne
         </a>
         , who was crowned as "Roman Emperor" by the
         <a href="/wiki/Pope_Leo_III" title="Pope Leo III">
          pope Leo III
         </a>
         in the year 800 in opposition to the
         <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">
          Roman Empire in the east
         </a>
         at the time being ruled by
         <a href="/wiki/Irene_of_Athens" title="Irene of Athens">
          Irene
         </a>
         , a woman.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In addition to remaining as a concept for an administrative unit in the
       <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">
        remaining Empire
       </a>
       , the ideal of the Roman Empire as a mighty Christian Empire with a single ruler further continued to appeal to many powerful rulers in western Europe. With the papal coronation of
       <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">
        Charlemagne
       </a>
       as "
       <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Holy Roman Emperor">
        Emperor of the Romans
       </a>
       " in 800 AD, his realm was explicitly proclaimed as a restoration of the Roman Empire in Western Europe under the concept of
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Translatio_imperii" title="Translatio imperii">
         translatio imperii
        </a>
       </i>
       . Though the
       <a href="/wiki/Carolingian_Empire" title="Carolingian Empire">
        Carolingian Empire
       </a>
       collapsed in 888 and
       <a href="/wiki/Berengar_I_of_Italy" title="Berengar I of Italy">
        Berengar
       </a>
       , the last "Emperor" claiming succession from Charlemagne, died in 924, the concept of a papacy- and Germanic-based Roman Empire in the West would resurface in the form of the
       <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">
        Holy Roman Empire
       </a>
       in 962. This Empire would regard itself as the successor state of
       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">
        Ancient Rome
       </a>
       until its downfall in 1806.
      </p>
      <p>
       Charlemagne, and the subsequent Holy Roman Emperors were not, and did not claim to be, rulers of a restored Western Roman Empire. Pope Leo III and contemporary historians were fully aware of that the notion of a separate Western court had been abolished over three centuries prior and considered the Roman Empire to be "one and indivisible". The ruler of the Roman Empire at the time of Charlemagne's coronation was
       <a href="/wiki/Irene_of_Athens" title="Irene of Athens">
        Irene
       </a>
       , the mother of emperor
       <a href="/wiki/Constantine_VI" title="Constantine VI">
        Constantine VI
       </a>
       who she had deposed. Leo III considered Irene to be a usurper and illegitimate to rule due to her gender and as such considered the imperial throne to be vacant. Thus, Charlemagne was not crowned as the ruler of the Western Roman Empire and successor to
       <a href="/wiki/Romulus_Augustulus" title="Romulus Augustulus">
        Romulus Augustulus
       </a>
       , but rather as the successor of Constantine VI and as sole Roman Emperor.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">
        <a href="#cite_note-121">
         [120]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Irene was deposed and replaced by Emperor
       <a href="/wiki/Nikephoros_I" title="Nikephoros I">
        Nikephoros
       </a>
       soon after, and the Eastern Empire refused to recognize the Imperial title of Charlemagne. Emperor
       <a href="/wiki/Michael_I_Rangabe" title="Michael I Rangabe">
        Michael I Rangabe
       </a>
       eventually recognized Charlemagne as an "Emperor"
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">
        <a href="#cite_note-122">
         [121]
        </a>
       </sup>
       following several wars in the 810s, but as the slightly humiliating "Emperor of the Franks" rather than "Roman Emperor", a title he reserved for himself.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">
        <a href="#cite_note-123">
         [122]
        </a>
       </sup>
       For centuries to come, the "revived" Western court and the Eastern court, in direct succession to the Roman Emperors of old, would make competing claims to be rulers of the whole and as being the sole legitimate Roman Empire.
      </p>
      <p>
       Following the final fall of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Roman_empire" title="Eastern Roman empire">
        Eastern Roman Empire
       </a>
       after the
       <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_Constantinople" title="Fall of Constantinople">
        Fall of Constantinople
       </a>
       in 1453 and the downfall of the
       <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">
        Holy Roman Empire
       </a>
       in 1806, the title of "Emperor" became widespread among European monarchs. The
       <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Empire" title="Austrian Empire">
        Austrian Empire
       </a>
       laid claim to be the heir of the Holy Roman Empire as Austria's
       <a href="/wiki/House_of_Habsburg" title="House of Habsburg">
        Habsburgs
       </a>
       attempted to unite Germany under their rule.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Craig_M._White_2007._P._139_124-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Craig_M._White_2007._P._139-124">
         [123]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">
        German Empire
       </a>
       , established in 1871, also claimed to be a successor of Rome through the lineage of the Holy Roman Empire.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Warwick_Ball_2000._P._449_125-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Warwick_Ball_2000._P._449-125">
         [124]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Both of these empires used the imperial title
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Kaiser" title="Kaiser">
         Kaiser
        </a>
       </i>
       (derived from Latin Caesar), the German word for emperor.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="List_of_Western_Roman_Emperors">

       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">

        </span>
       </span>

       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">

        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>

        </a>
        : 306 to 337
        <i>
         Sole emperor of the empire from 324 to 337
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Constantine_II_(emperor)" title="Constantine II (emperor)">
         Constantine II
        </a>
        : 337 to 340
        <i>

        </i>
       </li>

         Constantius II
        </a>

        <i>
         Emperor of the east from 337 to 353, Sole emperor of the empire from 353 to 360
        </i>
       </li>

        </a>

        </i>

         Julian
        </a>

        <i>
         Emperor of the west from 355 to 361, Sole emperor of the empire from 361 to 363
        </i>
       </li>
      </ul>

           </a>

          </i>

          </i>

        </ul>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Valentinian_III" title="Valentinian III">
         Valentinian III
        </a>
        : 423 to 455
        <ul>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Galla_Placidia" title="Galla Placidia">
           Galla Placidia
          </a>
          : 423 to 433
          <i>
           Regent
          </i>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flavius_A%C3%ABtius" title="Flavius Aëtius">
           Aëtius
          </a>
          : 433 to 454
          <i>
           Regent
          </i>
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span id="Non-dynastic_.28455_to_480.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Non-dynastic_(455_to_480)">
        Non-dynastic (455 to 480)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Western_Roman_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Non-dynastic (455 to 480)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Petronius_Maximus" title="Petronius Maximus">
         Petronius Maximus
        </a>
        : 455
        <i>
         not recognized in Constantinople
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Avitus" title="Avitus">
         Avitus
        </a>
        : 455 to 456
        <i>
         not recognized in Constantinople
        </i>
        <ul>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Ricimer" title="Ricimer">
           Ricimer
          </a>
          : 456 to 472
          <i>
           Power behind the throne
          </i>
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Majorian" title="Majorian">
         Majorian
        </a>
        : 457 to 461
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Libius_Severus" title="Libius Severus">
         Libius Severus
        </a>
        : 461 to 465
        <i>
         not recognized in Constantinople
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Anthemius" title="Anthemius">
         Anthemius
        </a>
        : 467 to 472
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Olybrius" title="Olybrius">
         Olybrius
        </a>
        : 472
        <i>
         not recognized in Constantinople
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Glycerius" title="Glycerius">
         Glycerius
        </a>
        : 473 to 474
        <i>
         not recognized in Constantinople
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Julius_Nepos" title="Julius Nepos">
         Julius Nepos
        </a>
        : 474 to 480
        <i>
         In exile 475 to 480
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Romulus_Augustus" title="Romulus Augustus">
         Romulus Augustus
        </a>
        : 475 to 476
        <i>
         not recognized in Constantinople
        </i>
        <ul>
         <li>
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flavius_Orestes" title="Flavius Orestes">
           Flavius Orestes
          </a>
          : 475 to 476
          <i>
           Power behind the throne
          </i>
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Flavius Orestes was killed by revolting Germanic
       <a href="/wiki/Mercenary" title="Mercenary">
        mercenaries
       </a>
       . Their chieftain,
       <a href="/wiki/Odoacer" title="Odoacer">
        Odoacer
       </a>
       , assumed control of Italy as a
       <a href="/wiki/De_jure" title="De jure">
        de jure
       </a>
       representative of Julius Nepos and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Roman_Emperor" title="Eastern Roman Emperor">
        Eastern Roman Emperor
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Zeno_(emperor)" title="Zeno (emperor)">
        Zeno
       </a>
       .
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Notes_2">
        Notes
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Western_Roman_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Notes">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="mw-references-wrap">
       <ol class="references">
        <li id="cite_note-108">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-108">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <a href="/wiki/Ecclesiastical_Latin" title="Ecclesiastical Latin">
           Ecclesiastical Latin
          </a>
          , the language used by the modern
          <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">
           Catholic Church
          </a>
          , is largely identical to written
          <a href="/wiki/Classical_Latin" title="Classical Latin">
           Classical Latin
          </a>
          (the language of the Roman Empire), but differs in a simplified syntax and a pronunciation that is closer to modern
          <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">
           Italian
          </a>
          than to the language of antiquity.
         </span>
        </li>
       </ol>
      </div>
